# **COMPREHENSIVE ENGLISH GRAMMAR - LEVEL 3 SYNTAX**

---

### **SYNTAX (Sentence Structure)**

│
├── **I. Sentence**
│   │
│   ├── **A. Internal Structure**
│   │   │
│   │   ├── **1. Clause**
│   │   │   │
│   │   │   ├── **a. Clause Types by Independence**
│   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   ├── **i. Independent Clause (Main Clause)**
│   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Definition:**
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── A complete grammatical unit that can stand alone as a sentence
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── Expresses a complete thought with full semantic meaning
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── Also called "matrix clause" or "superordinate clause" in formal linguistics
│   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Essential Requirements:**
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **1. Subject** (explicit or implied in imperatives)
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **2. Finite Verb** (marked for tense and agreement)
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **3. Complete Meaning** (not syntactically dependent on another clause)
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── **4. No Subordinating Marker** (no subordinating conjunction at the start)
│   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Structure Patterns:**
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **SV:** "Birds **fly**." / "The sun **shines**."
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **SVO:** "She **reads** books." / "They **built** a house."
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **SVC:** "He **is** happy." / "She **became** a doctor."
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **SVOO:** "She **gave** him a book." / "I **told** them the news."
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── **SVOC:** "They **elected** him president." / "She **considered** it wrong."
│   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Examples by Complexity:**
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **Simple:** "**The cat sleeps on the mat.**"
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **With Dependent:** "**I left** because I was tired." (main = "I left")
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **With Embedded:** "**I know** that she is coming." (main = "I know")
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── **Multiple Embedding:** "**I believe** that he knows what she wants."
│   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Types by Internal Structure:**
│   │   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **(1) Simple Main Clause**
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   ├── Contains no embedded clauses
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   ├── "The cat sleeps." / "She wrote a letter yesterday."
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   └── May have complex phrases: "The very old man in the corner smiled."
│   │   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── **(2) Main Clause with Subordination**
│   │   │   │   │   │       ├── Contains one or more dependent clauses
│   │   │   │   │   │       ├── "**I know** [that she left]." (with noun clause)
│   │   │   │   │   │       ├── "**The man** [who came] **is here**." (with relative clause)
│   │   │   │   │   │       └── "**She smiled** [when she saw him]." (with adverbial clause)
│   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Sentence Types (Functional Classification):**
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **Declarative:** Makes a statement - "She is a teacher."
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   └── Word Order: S + V + (O/C) + (Adjunct)
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **Interrogative:** Asks a question
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   ├── Yes/No: "**Is** she a teacher?" (Aux-S inversion)
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   ├── Wh-question: "**What** does she do?" (Wh-word + Aux-S inversion)
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   └── Tag: "She's a teacher, **isn't she**?"
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **Imperative:** Gives a command
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   ├── "**Close** the door!" (implied subject 'you')
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   ├── "**Let's** go!" (1st person inclusive)
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   └── "**Do** be careful!" (emphatic)
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── **Exclamative:** Expresses strong emotion
│   │   │   │   │   │       ├── "**What** a beautiful day (it is)!"
│   │   │   │   │   │       ├── "**How** quickly she runs!"
│   │   │   │   │   │       └── Always introduced by what/how
│   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Key Grammatical Properties:**
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **Tense Marking:** Verb shows past/present distinction
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   └── "She **writes**." (present) / "She **wrote**." (past)
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **Subject-Verb Agreement:** Verb agrees with subject
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   └── "He **runs**." / "They **run**." / "I **am**." / "She **is**."
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **Mood Selection:** Indicative, Subjunctive, Imperative
│   │   │   │   │   │   │   └── "She **is**." / "I demand that she **be**." / "**Be** quiet!"
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── **Polarity:** Can be affirmative or negative
│   │   │   │   │   │       └── "She came." / "She **did not** come."
│   │   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   │   └── **Coordination of Independent Clauses:**
│   │   │   │   │       ├── **Coordinating Conjunctions (FANBOYS):**
│   │   │   │   │       │   ├── **For** (reason): "She left early, **for** she was tired."
│   │   │   │   │       │   ├── **And** (addition): "He sang, **and** she danced."
│   │   │   │   │       │   ├── **Nor** (negative): "He didn't call, **nor** did he write."
│   │   │   │   │       │   ├── **But** (contrast): "She tried, **but** she failed."
│   │   │   │   │       │   ├── **Or** (alternative): "Leave now, **or** miss the train."
│   │   │   │   │       │   ├── **Yet** (contrast): "It's small, **yet** it's powerful."
│   │   │   │   │       │   └── **So** (result): "It rained, **so** we stayed home."
│   │   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │   │       ├── **Punctuation Rules:**
│   │   │   │   │       │   ├── ✔ Comma + conjunction: "She sang, and he danced."
│   │   │   │   │       │   ├── ✔ Semicolon alone: "She sang; he danced."
│   │   │   │   │       │   ├── ✘ Comma alone (comma splice): "She sang, he danced."
│   │   │   │   │       │   └── ✘ Nothing (run-on): "She sang he danced."
│   │   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │   │       └── **Conjunctive Adverbs:** (Use semicolon before, comma after)
│   │   │   │   │           ├── "She failed; **however**, she tried again."
│   │   │   │   │           ├── "He's smart; **moreover**, he's hardworking."
│   │   │   │   │           └── Common: however, therefore, moreover, nevertheless, consequently
│   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   └── **ii. Dependent Clause (Subordinate Clause)**
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       ├── **Definition:**
│   │   │   │       │   ├── A clause that cannot stand alone as a complete sentence
│   │   │   │       │   ├── Grammatically depends on a main clause for meaning
│   │   │   │       │   ├── Functions as a noun, adjective, or adverb within the sentence
│   │   │   │       │   └── Also called "embedded clause" or "subordinate clause"
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       ├── **Markers of Subordination:**
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Subordinating Conjunctions:** because, if, when, while, although, since, unless
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Relative Pronouns:** who, whom, whose, which, that
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Relative Adverbs:** where, when, why, how
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Wh-words:** what, who, which, when, where, why, how
│   │   │   │       │   └── **Complementizers:** that, if, whether, for (in for-to infinitives)
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       ├── **General Properties:**
│   │   │   │       │   ├── Cannot function as complete sentence (*"Because he was tired.")
│   │   │   │       │   ├── Must attach to independent clause
│   │   │   │       │   ├── Can be finite or non-finite
│   │   │   │       │   └── Position varies: initial, medial, or final
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       ├── **(1) Noun Clause (Nominal Clause)**
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Definition:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── A dependent clause functioning as a noun
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── Can occupy any position a noun phrase would
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── Also called "nominal clause" or "content clause"
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Introducers:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **That:** "I know **that** she is here." (declarative content)
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Whether/If:** "I wonder **whether** he'll come." (polar question)
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Wh-words:** "I know **what** she wants." (embedded question)
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Whoever/Whatever/etc.:** "**Whoever** comes is welcome." (free relatives)
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── **Zero (Ø):** "I think [Ø] she left." (that-deletion)
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Syntactic Functions:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **(a) Subject:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "**That he lied** is obvious." (that-clause)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "**What she said** shocked everyone." (wh-clause)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "**Whether he'll come** is uncertain." (if/whether-clause)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "**Whoever wins** will get the prize." (free relative)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── Often extraposed: "**It** is obvious **that he lied**."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **(b) Direct Object:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "I believe **that she is honest**." (that-clause)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "I wonder **what he wants**." (wh-clause)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "She asked **whether I could help**." (if/whether)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── "I'll take **whatever you give me**." (free relative)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **(c) Subject Complement (Predicative):**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "The truth is **that he knew all along**."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "The problem is **what we should do next**."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── "Her question was **whether he would agree**."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **(d) Object of Preposition:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "She was surprised at **what he said**."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "I'm curious about **whether it works**."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── "The prize goes to **whoever finishes first**."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── **(e) Appositive:**
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── "The fact **that he lied** shocked us."
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── "The idea **that earth is flat** is wrong."
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── "Her claim **that she was innocent** was false."
│   │   │   │       │   │       └── **Note:** Renames/explains the preceding noun
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Types of Noun Clauses:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **(a) That-clause (Declarative Content Clause):**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Function:** Introduces factual/believed propositions or content
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples with 'that':**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "I believe **that she is honest**." (object position)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "He said **that he would come**." (object position)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **That-deletion rules:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── ✔ **Deletable** (informal) in object position: "I think [Ø] she left." = "I think **that** she left."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── ✘ **NOT deletable** in these situations:
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │       ├── Subject position: ✘ "*He lied is obvious." → ✔ "**That** he lied is obvious."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │       ├── Appositive: ✘ "*The fact he lied" → ✔ "The fact **that** he lied"
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │       ├── After adjective: ✘ "*I'm sure he came" → ✔ "I'm sure **that** he came"
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │       └── When ambiguous: ✘ "*She said on Tuesday he left" → ✔ "She said **that** on Tuesday he left"
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **(b) Wh-clause (Embedded Question/Exclamative):**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Embedded Question (Indirect Question):**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Structure:** Uses statement word order (NOT question inversion)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "I wonder **what he wants**." (declarative word order, not "what does he want")
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "Do you know **where she lives**?" (statement order inside question)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "Tell me **how it works**." (statement order)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── **Common error:** ✘ "I know **what does he want**." → ✔ "I know **what he wants**."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Embedded Exclamative:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       ├── "You won't believe **what a mess he made**!" (expresses speaker's emotion/surprise)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       ├── "I showed her **how beautifully it sings**." (emphasizes degree/manner)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       └── **Structure:** Similar to embedded question but expresses exclamation (intensity)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **(c) If/Whether-clause (Polar Question Content):**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Function:** Presents two-way choice (yes/no questions converted to embedded form)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "I don't know **if/whether he's coming**." (is he coming? yes or no)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "She wondered **whether to go or stay**." (should she go? should she stay?)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Whether vs. If - Distribution rules:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── Both acceptable after most verbs: know, wonder, ask, doubt
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   │   └── "I know **if/whether** she's coming."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── ONLY 'whether' in subject position: "**Whether** he comes is uncertain." (not *if)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── ONLY 'whether' after preposition: "about **whether**" / "on **whether**" (not *if)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── ONLY 'whether' with 'or not' immediately after: "**whether or not**" (not *if or not)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Example:** "I wonder **whether or not** he'll agree." vs. ✘ "I wonder if or not he'll agree."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── **(d) Free Relative Clause (Headless Relative):**
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── **Definition:** A relative clause without an explicit head noun
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── The wh-word combines both the relative pronoun and antecedent meaning
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── Example meanings:
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── "**Whoever** comes is welcome." (= any person who comes)
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── "I'll eat **whatever** you cook." (= any food/thing that you cook)
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── "Go **wherever** you want." (= to any place where you want to go)
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   └── "**However** you do it is fine." (= in any manner/way in which you do it)
│   │   │   │       │   │       └── **Words used:** whoever, whatever, whichever, wherever, whenever, however
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **That-Deletion Rules:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Deletable (informal):**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── Object position: "I think (that) she left."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── After common verbs: think, say, know, believe, hope, wish
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── Short clauses: "I know (that) it's true."
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── **Not Deletable:**
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── Subject position: "**That** he lied is clear." (not *He lied is clear)
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── Appositive: "The fact **that** he lied..." (not *The fact he lied)
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── After adjective: "I'm happy **that** she came."
│   │   │   │       │   │       └── When ambiguous: "She said **that** on Tuesday he left."
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Subjunctive in Noun Clauses:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Mandative Subjunctive:** (Formal English, especially AmE)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "I demand that he **be** present." (not *is)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "She suggested that he **go**." (not *goes)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── "It's important that she **arrive** on time."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── After: demand, insist, recommend, suggest, require, propose
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── **Alternative (BrE):** Use 'should' + base verb
│   │   │   │       │   │       └── "I suggest that he **should go**."
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   └── **Common Exam Traps:**
│   │   │   │       │       ├── ✘ Word order error: "I wonder **where is she**." → ✔ "where **she is**"
│   │   │   │       │       ├── ✘ Wrong complementizer: "*I don't know **that** he's coming or not."
│   │   │   │       │       ├── ✘ Subjunctive error: "I demand that he **is** here." → ✔ "**be** here"
│   │   │   │       │       └── ✘ Inappropriate that-deletion: "*The fact he lied shocked us."
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       ├── **(2) Adjective Clause (Relative Clause)**
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Definition:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── A dependent clause that modifies a noun or pronoun
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── Describes, identifies, or gives extra information about antecedent
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── Also called "relative clause" or "attributive clause"
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Introducers (Relative Words):**
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Relative Pronouns:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Who:** Subject (human) - "The man **who** came..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Whom:** Object (human, formal) - "The man **whom** I saw..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Which:** Subject/Object (non-human) - "The book **which** I read..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **That:** Subject/Object (human/non-human) - "The person **that** called..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Whose:** Possessive (human/non-human) - "The man **whose** car..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── **Relative Adverbs:**
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── **Where:** Indicates place - "The house **where** I grew up..."
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   └── Formal equivalent: "The house **in which** I grew up..."
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── **When:** Indicates time - "The day **when** we met..."
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   └── Formal equivalent: "The day **on which** we met..." or "The day **that** we met..."
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── **Why:** Indicates reason - "The reason **why** he left..." (often omitted in modern English)
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   └── Often just: "The reason he left..." or "The reason that he left..."
│   │   │   │       │   │       └── **Note:** Modern English increasingly allows omission or substitution of these relative adverbs
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Types:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **(a) Defining (Restrictive) Relative Clause:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── Identifies or restricts the noun (essential for meaning)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── Specifies WHICH one among possible referents
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── Removing it changes the meaning significantly
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Punctuation:** NO COMMAS
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── ✔ "The students who study hard succeed."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "The book **that I read** was excellent." (specific book)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "Students **who study hard** usually succeed." (only those who study)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "The house **where she lives** is old." (identifies which house)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "The reason **why he left** is unknown." (specific reason)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Relative Word Choice:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── **'That' preferred** in defining/restrictive clauses (especially after superlatives: the best **that** ever was)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── **'Who/Which'** also acceptable in defining clauses
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── **Zero Relative (Contact Clause):** Relativizer omitted when object of clause
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │       ├── ✔ "The book [Ø] I read..." = "The book **that** I read..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │       ├── ✔ "The person [Ø] you met..." = "The person **who** you met..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │       └── **Why allowed:** Listener can infer the omitted relative pronoun from syntax
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Contact Clause (Zero Relative) - DETAILED:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       ├── **Rule:** Relative pronoun omitted ONLY when it's the OBJECT of relative clause
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       ├── **Grammatical condition:** Listener must be able to infer missing pronoun from syntax
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       ├── **Allowed examples:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       │   ├── ✔ "The man [Ø] I saw..." (man = object of 'saw'; who/that can be omitted)
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       │   ├── ✔ "The book [Ø] she wrote..." (book = object of 'wrote')
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       │   └── ✔ "The person [Ø] we met..." (person = object of 'met')
│   │   │   │       │   │   │       └── **NOT allowed:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │           ├── ✘ "*The man [Ø] came..." (man = SUBJECT of 'came' → MUST say "who came")
│   │   │   │       │   │   │           ├── ✘ "*The book [Ø] sits on the shelf..." (book = SUBJECT → MUST say "that sits")
│   │   │   │       │   │   │           └── **Why?** Omitting subject relative pronoun creates ambiguous or ungrammatical structure
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── **(b) Non-defining (Non-restrictive) Relative Clause:**
│   │   │   │       │   │       │
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── **Definition:**
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── Adds EXTRA information (not essential for identification)
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── Antecedent is already uniquely identified
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── Removing it doesn't change core meaning
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   └── Like a parenthetical insertion
│   │   │   │       │   │       │
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── **Punctuation:** MUST USE COMMAS
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   └── ✔ "My brother**,** who lives in Paris**,** is visiting."
│   │   │   │       │   │       │
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── "My brother**,** **who lives in Paris,** is visiting." (only one brother)
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── "London**,** **which is the capital,** is very old." (only one London)
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── "Shakespeare**,** **who wrote Hamlet,** was English." (unique person)
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   └── "Yesterday**,** **when we met,** was memorable." (specific day)
│   │   │   │       │   │       │
│   │   │   │       │   │       ├── **Important Restrictions:**
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── ✘ CANNOT use 'that': "*London, **that** is the capital..."
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   ├── ✘ CANNOT omit relative pronoun: "*My brother, lives in Paris, is..."
│   │   │   │       │   │       │   └── Must use who/whom/which/where/when/whose only
│   │   │   │       │   │       │
│   │   │   │       │   │       └── **Sentential Relative Clause:**
│   │   │   │       │   │           ├── 'Which' refers to entire preceding clause (not a noun)
│   │   │   │       │   │           ├── "He passed the exam**,** **which** surprised everyone."
│   │   │   │       │   │           ├── "She resigned**,** **which** caused quite a stir."
│   │   │   │       │   │           └── Always non-restrictive; always uses 'which'
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Relative Pronoun Functions in Clause:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Subject:** "The man **who** came..." (who = subject of 'came')
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Direct Object:** "The man **whom** I saw..." (whom = object of 'saw')
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Object of Preposition:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── Formal: "The man **to whom** I spoke..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── Informal: "The man **who** I spoke **to**..." (stranded prep)
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Possessive:** "The man **whose** car was stolen..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── **Adverbial:** "The place **where** I live..." / "The time **when** we met..."
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Preposition Placement:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Formal (Fronted):** "The woman **to whom** I spoke is my boss."
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Informal (Stranded):** "The woman **who** I spoke **to** is my boss."
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── Fronted requires 'whom' (not 'who') for human objects
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── Stranded allows 'who' or null: "The woman [Ø] I spoke to..."
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Special Constructions:**
│   │   │   │       │   │   ├── **Reduced Relative Clause (Participle Phrase):**
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── Present: "The man **sitting there**..." = "who is sitting..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   ├── Past: "The book **written by her**..." = "which was written..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │   └── Infinitive: "The first person **to arrive**..." = "who arrived first..."
│   │   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │   │       │   │   └── **Stacked/Multiple Relatives:**
│   │   │   │       │   │       └── "The man **who lives here** **who(m) I mentioned** is my uncle."
│   │   │   │       │   │
│   │   │   │       │   └── **Common Exam Traps:**
│   │   │   │       │       ├── ✘ Using 'that' in non-restrictive: "*Paris, **that** is beautiful..."
│   │   │   │       │       ├── ✘ Missing commas in non-restrictive: "*My brother who lives in Paris is..."
│   │   │   │       │       ├── ✘ Wrong relative for possessive: "*The man **who's** car..." → **whose**
│   │   │   │       │       ├── ✘ Omitting subject relative: "*The man came is here." → "who came"
│   │   │   │       │       └── ✘ Case error: "*The man **who** I spoke to..." (formal: **whom**)
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       └── **(3) Adverbial Clause**
│   │   │   │           │
│   │   │   │           ├── **Definition:**
│   │   │   │           │   ├── A dependent clause functioning as an adverb
│   │   │   │           │   ├── Modifies a verb, adjective, other adverb, or entire clause
│   │   │   │           │   ├── Expresses circumstance: time, place, manner, reason, etc.
│   │   │   │           │   └── Also called "adverb clause" or "adjunct clause"
│   │   │   │           │
│   │   │   │           ├── **Position Flexibility:**
│   │   │   │           │   ├── **Initial (Front):** "**When she arrived**, we left." (+ comma)
│   │   │   │           │   ├── **Final (End):** "We left **when she arrived**." (usually no comma)
│   │   │   │           │   └── **Medial (Mid):** "We, **when she arrived**, left." (rare, with commas)
│   │   │   │           │
│   │   │   │           ├── **General Properties:**
│   │   │   │           │   ├── Introduced by subordinating conjunction
│   │   │   │           │   ├── Usually optional (adjuncts, not complements)
│   │   │   │           │   ├── Can be finite or non-finite (reduced)
│   │   │   │           │   └── Answers questions: When? Where? Why? How? Under what condition?
│   │   │   │           │
│   │   │   │           └── **Types by Semantic Function:**
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               ├── **(a) Time Clause (Temporal):**
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Conjunctions:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Simultaneity:** when, while, as, whenever
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Sequence:** before, after, since, until/till
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Immediate:** as soon as, the moment, once, no sooner...than
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── **Duration:** while, as long as
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**When** she arrived, we left."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**While** you were sleeping, I called."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**After** she left, we relaxed."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**Since** he came, things have changed." (point in time)
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "I'll wait **until** you're ready."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── "**As soon as** I saw her, I smiled."
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Tense Rules:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── Future in main → Present in time clause
│   │   │   │               │   │   │   └── "I'll call you **when** I **arrive**." (not *will arrive)
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── Future perfect sense → Present perfect
│   │   │   │               │   │       └── "I'll call **after** I **have finished**."
│   │   │   │               │   └── **Inversion patterns:**
│   │   │   │               │       └── "**No sooner** had she arrived **than** we left."
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               ├── **(b) Place Clause (Locative):**
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Conjunctions:** where, wherever, everywhere
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**Wherever** you go, I'll follow."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "Stay **where** you are."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**Everywhere** she looked, there were flowers."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── "Put it back **where** you found it."
│   │   │   │               │   └── **Note:** 'Where' can also introduce noun clauses
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               ├── **(c) Manner Clause:**
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Conjunctions:** as, as if, as though, (the way)
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "Do it **as** I showed you." (actual manner)
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "He acts **as if** he knows everything." (hypothetical)
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "She looked at me **as though** she'd seen a ghost."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── "Do it **(the way)** I taught you."
│   │   │   │               │   └── **'As if/as though' + Past Tense (Hypothetical):**
│   │   │   │               │       ├── "He talks **as if** he **were** (subjunctive) the boss."
│   │   │   │               │       └── Indicates unreal/contrary-to-fact situation
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               ├── **(d) Reason/Cause Clause:**
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Conjunctions:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Because:** Direct cause (strongest) - "He left **because** he was tired."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Since:** Background reason (known) - "**Since** you're here, let's start."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **As:** Background reason (weaker) - "**As** it was late, we left."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **For:** (Archaic/literary) - "He left, **for** he was tired."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── **Now that/Given that:** - "**Now that** you mention it..."
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**Because** he was ill, he stayed home."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**Since** everyone is here, we can begin."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── "I trust her, **for** she has never lied."
│   │   │   │               │   └── **Position:**
│   │   │   │               │       ├── 'Because' clause usually final: "He left **because** he was tired."
│   │   │   │               │       └── 'Since/As' clause often initial: "**Since** it's late, let's go."
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               ├── **(e) Purpose Clause:**
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Conjunctions:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **So that:** "I studied **so that** I would pass."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **In order that:** (Formal) "**In order that** he might succeed..."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Lest:** (Formal/archaic) "Take notes **lest** you forget."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── **For fear that:** "Speak softly **for fear that** he might hear."
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Structure Notes:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── Often contain modal: may, might, could, would, should
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "She left early **so that** she **could** catch the train."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── Non-finite alternative: "She left early **to catch** the train."
│   │   │   │               │   └── **Negative Purpose:**
│   │   │   │               │       ├── "She whispered **so that** they **wouldn't** hear."
│   │   │   │               │       └── "He ran **lest** he **be** late." (subjunctive with 'lest')
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               ├── **(f) Result Clause (Consecutive):**
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Structure:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **So + adj/adv + that:** "He was **so** tired **that** he slept."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Such + noun/NP + that:** "It was **such** a good book **that** I read it twice."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── **So much/many + that:** "He had **so many** problems **that** he quit."
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "The storm was **so** violent **that** trees fell."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "She spoke **so** quietly **that** no one heard."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "It was **such** a surprise **that** I screamed."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── "There was **so much** noise **that** we couldn't talk."
│   │   │   │               │   └── **Purpose vs. Result:**
│   │   │   │               │       ├── Purpose: "He studied hard **so that** he **would** pass." (intended)
│   │   │   │               │       └── Result: "He studied **so** hard **that** he **passed**." (actual outcome)
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               ├── **(g) Condition Clause (Conditional):**
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Conjunctions:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **If:** Most common - "**If** you come, I'll be happy."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Unless:** Negative condition - "**Unless** you hurry, you'll miss it."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Provided (that):** Formal - "**Provided that** you agree..."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **As long as:** Duration/condition - "**As long as** you're careful..."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **On condition that:** Very formal
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Supposing (that):** Hypothetical - "**Supposing** it rains..."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── **In case:** Precaution - "Take an umbrella **in case** it rains."
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Conditional Types:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Type 0 (Zero - General Truth):**
│   │   │   │               │   │   │   ├── Pattern: If + present, present
│   │   │   │               │   │   │   └── "**If** you heat ice, it **melts**."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Type 1 (Real - Likely Future):**
│   │   │   │               │   │   │   ├── Pattern: If + present, will + base
│   │   │   │               │   │   │   └── "**If** you come, I **will** be happy."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Type 2 (Unreal - Hypothetical Present/Future):**
│   │   │   │               │   │   │   ├── Pattern: If + past (were), would + base
│   │   │   │               │   │   │   └── "**If** I **were** rich, I **would** travel."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── **Type 3 (Unreal - Hypothetical Past):**
│   │   │   │               │   │       ├── Pattern: If + past perfect, would have + past participle
│   │   │   │               │   │       └── "**If** I **had known**, I **would have helped**."
│   │   │   │               │   └── **Inversion (Formal, no 'if'):**
│   │   │   │               │       ├── "**Were** I rich, I would travel." (= If I were)
│   │   │   │               │       ├── "**Had** I known, I would have helped." (= If I had known)
│   │   │   │               │       └── "**Should** you need help, call me." (= If you should)
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               ├── **(h) Concession Clause (Contrasting):**
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Conjunctions:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Although/Though/Even though:** "**Although** it rained, we went."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **While:** Contrast - "**While** I like him, I don't trust him."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Whereas:** Opposition - "He is tall, **whereas** she is short."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Even if:** Hypothetical concession - "**Even if** he came, I'd leave."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **No matter + wh-:** "**No matter what** you say..."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── **However + adj/adv:** "**However hard** he tries..."
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**Although** it was expensive, I bought it."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**Even though** he apologized, she didn't forgive him."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**However** difficult it is, I'll try."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── "**No matter where** you go, I'll find you."
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Word Order Notes:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── 'Though' can come at end (informal): "It was hard, **though**."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── Inversion with 'though': "**Hard though** it was, I finished."
│   │   │   │               │   └── **Difference from 'but':**
│   │   │   │               │       ├── 'Although' = subordinating (begins dependent clause)
│   │   │   │               │       └── 'But' = coordinating (joins independent clauses)
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               ├── **(i) Comparison Clause:**
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Structures:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **As...as (Equal):** "She is **as** tall **as** I am."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Not as/so...as (Unequal):** "He's **not as** smart **as** she is."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **-er/more...than (Superior):** "She runs faster **than** I do."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── **Less...than (Inferior):** "He is **less** patient **than** her."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── **The more...the more (Proportion):** "**The** more you practice, **the** better you get."
│   │   │   │               │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "She's taller **than** he is/him." (formal/informal)
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "I work **as** hard **as** you (do)."
│   │   │   │               │   │   ├── "**The** sooner you leave, **the** better."
│   │   │   │               │   │   └── "She knows more **than** I thought (she would)."
│   │   │   │               │   └── **Ellipsis:** Often reduced: "She's taller **than** me." (than I am)
│   │   │   │               │
│   │   │   │               └── **(j) Additional Minor Types:**
│   │   │   │                   │
│   │   │   │                   ├── **Degree Clause:**
│   │   │   │                   │   ├── Shows extent/degree
│   │   │   │                   │   └── "She worked **as hard as** she could."
│   │   │   │                   │
│   │   │   │                   ├── **Comment Clause:**
│   │   │   │                   │   ├── Parenthetical remark (speaker's attitude)
│   │   │   │                   │   ├── "He is, **as you know**, a liar."
│   │   │   │                   │   └── "**As far as I know**, he left."
│   │   │   │                   │
│   │   │   │                   └── **Proportion Clause:**
│   │   │   │                       ├── Parallel increase/decrease
│   │   │   │                       └── "**The more** I learn, **the less** I understand."
│   │   │   │
│   │   │   ├── **b. Clause Types by Verb Form (Finiteness)**
│   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   ├── **i. Finite Clause**
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Contains finite verb (marked for tense/agreement)
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Properties:**
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── Verb shows tense (past/present)
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── Subject-verb agreement
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── Can be negated with 'not' after auxiliary
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── "I know **that she is coming**." (that-clause)
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── "The man **who lives here**..." (relative)
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── "**Because he was tired**, he left." (adverbial)
│   │   │   │   │   └── **Types by Function:**
│   │   │   │   │       ├── **Declarative:** "She said [that he left]."
│   │   │   │   │       ├── **Interrogative:** "I wonder [if he came]."
│   │   │   │   │       └── **Exclamative:** "I told her [what a fool he is]!"
│   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   └── **ii. Non-finite Clause**
│   │   │   │       ├── **Definition:** Verb NOT marked for tense/agreement
│   │   │   │       ├── **Properties:**
│   │   │   │       │   ├── No tense marking on verb
│   │   │   │       │   ├── Subject often omitted (understood from context)
│   │   │   │       │   └── More compact than finite clauses
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       ├── **(1) Infinitive Clause (to + base verb)**
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Full infinitive:** "I want **to leave**."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **With subject:** "I want **him to leave**."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **For-to clause:** "**For him to leave** would be wrong."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Purpose:** "He came **to see** her."
│   │   │   │       │   └── **After adjectives:** "It is easy **to learn**."
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       ├── **(2) Bare Infinitive Clause (base verb, no 'to')**
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **After modals:** "She can **swim**."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **After causatives:** "Make him **go**." / "Let her **stay**."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **After perception:** "I saw him **run**."
│   │   │   │       │   └── **After 'help':** "Help me **carry** this." (optional to)
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       ├── **(3) Present Participle Clause (-ing clause)**
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Adverbial:** "**Walking home**, I saw her."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Adjectival:** "The man **sitting there** is my father."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Complement:** "I saw her **running**."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Subject:** "**Swimming daily** keeps you fit."
│   │   │   │       │   └── **With subject:** "**Him being late** annoyed everyone."
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       ├── **(4) Past Participle Clause (-ed/-en clause)**
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Adverbial:** "**Tired from work**, he slept early."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Adjectival:** "The book **written by her** is famous."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── **Complement:** "I found the door **locked**."
│   │   │   │       │   └── **Absolute:** "**The work finished**, they relaxed."
│   │   │   │       │
│   │   │   │       └── **(5) Verbless Clause (Reduced/Minor Clause)**
│   │   │   │           ├── **Definition:** Clause with understood/implied verb
│   │   │   │           ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │           │   ├── "Although **[he was] tired**, he continued."
│   │   │   │           │   ├── "If **[it is] possible**, please help."
│   │   │   │           │   ├── "When **[you are] in Rome**, do as Romans do."
│   │   │   │           │   └── "**Whether right or wrong**, I'll support you."
│   │   │   │           └── **Common with:** although, if, when, while, whether
│   │   │   │
│   │   │   ├── **c. Clause Types by Syntactic Role**
│   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   ├── **i. Matrix Clause (Root Clause)**
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** The outermost clause containing all others
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Example:** "**[I think** that she knows what he wants**]**."
│   │   │   │   │   └── **Note:** Always an independent clause
│   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   ├── **ii. Embedded Clause**
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Clause contained within another clause
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Types:**
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **Complement clause:** "I know [**that she left**]."
│   │   │   │   │   │   ├── **Relative clause:** "The man [**who came**]..."
│   │   │   │   │   │   └── **Multiple embedding:** "I think [that she knows [what he wants]]."
│   │   │   │   │   └── **Note:** Can be finite or non-finite
│   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   ├── **iii. Adjunct Clause (Adverbial)**
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Optional modifier clause (can be removed)
│   │   │   │   │   ├── **Example:** "He left, [**because he was tired**]."
│   │   │   │   │   └── **vs. Complement:** Adjuncts are optional; complements required
│   │   │   │   │
│   │   │   │   └── **iv. Small Clause (Verbless Predication)**
│   │   │   │       ├── **Definition:** Predication without finite verb
│   │   │   │       ├── **Structure:** NP + Predicate (no inflected verb)
│   │   │   │       ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │   │       │   ├── "I consider [**him honest**]." (him = subj, honest = pred)
│   │   │   │       │   ├── "She found [**the door open**]."
│   │   │   │       │   ├── "With [**the lights off**], we slept."
│   │   │   │       │   └── "I want [**him gone**]."
│   │   │   │       └── **Predicates:** Adjective, PP, NP, past participle
│   │   │   │
│   │   │   └── **d. Clause Elements**
│   │   │       │
│   │   │       ├── **i. Subject (S)**
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   ├── **A. Definition & Identification**
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(1) Definition:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── The entity about which the predicate makes a statement
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── Typically the doer/agent of the action or topic of the sentence
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── Grammatically required in English (unlike pro-drop languages)
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(2) Identification Tests:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Question Test:** Ask "WHO/WHAT + verb?"
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "**The cat** sleeps." → What sleeps? = The cat
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Position Test:** Typically before finite verb (in declaratives)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── S + V + (O) = canonical English order
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Agreement Test:** Subject determines verb agreement
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "He **runs**." (3rd sg) / "They **run**." (plural)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── Verb inflection matches subject's person/number
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Tag Question Test:** Subject appears in tag
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "**John** came, didn't **he**?"
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Passive Test:** Subject of passive = Object of active
│   │   │       │   │   │       └── "The book was read [by her]." → book = subject
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   └── **(3) Case Requirement:**
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **Nominative/Subjective Case:** Required for pronouns
│   │   │       │   │       │   ├── ✔ "**He** runs." / "**She** is happy." / "**They** left."
│   │   │       │   │       │   └── ✘ "Him runs." / "Her is happy." / "Them left."
│   │   │       │   │       └── Pronouns: I, you, he, she, it, we, they, who, whoever
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   ├── **B. Forms/Elements of Subject (What Can Be a Subject)**
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(1) Noun Phrase (Most Common)**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Structure:** (Det) + (Adj*) + N + (PP/RC)*
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── Simple: "**The cat** sleeps."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── Complex: "**The big black cat on the mat** sleeps."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── Heavy: "**The cat that my neighbor bought last week** sleeps."
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Head Noun:** Core of NP determines agreement
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(2) Pronoun**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Personal:** "**She** runs." / "**They** left."
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Demonstrative:** "**This** is important." / "**Those** are mine."
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Indefinite:** "**Everyone** knows." / "**Something** happened."
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Interrogative:** "**Who** called?" / "**What** happened?"
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Relative:** "The man **who** came..." (subject of rel. clause)
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Reflexive (rare):** "**Myself**, I prefer tea." (emphatic only)
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(3) Gerund Phrase (V-ing as Noun)**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** -ing form functioning as noun
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**Swimming** is fun."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**Reading books** improves vocabulary."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "**His leaving early** surprised everyone."
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **With Possessive:** "**His coming** was unexpected." (formal)
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(4) Infinitive Phrase (to + V)**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** to-infinitive functioning as noun
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**To err** is human."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**To learn a language** takes time."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "**To be or not to be** is the question."
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Often extraposed:** "**It** is fun **to swim**." (It = placeholder)
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(5) That-Clause (Finite Nominal Clause)**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Clause introduced by 'that' as subject
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**That he lied** is obvious."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**That she won** surprised everyone."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "**Whether he comes** is uncertain."
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Often extraposed:** "**It** is obvious **that he lied**."
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(6) Wh-Clause (Embedded Question as Subject)**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**What he said** was shocking."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**Where she lives** remains unknown."
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "**How it happened** is a mystery."
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Free Relatives:** "**Whoever comes** will be welcome."
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   └── **(7) Dummy/Expletive Subject (Placeholder Subjects)**
│   │   │       │   │       │
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **(i) Expletive 'It' (Anticipatory Subject)**
│   │   │       │   │       │   ├── **Definition:** 'It' holding place for delayed clause
│   │   │       │   │       │   ├── **Types:**
│   │   │       │   │       │   │   ├── **Weather/Time:** "**It** is raining." / "**It** is 5 o'clock."
│   │   │       │   │       │   │   ├── **Distance:** "**It** is 10 miles to town."
│   │   │       │   │       │   │   ├── **Cleft:** "**It** was John who won."
│   │   │       │   │       │   │   └── **Extraposition:** "**It** is clear that he left."
│   │   │       │   │       │   └── **Test:** Cannot be questioned (*What is raining?)
│   │   │       │   │       │
│   │   │       │   │       └── **(ii) Expletive 'There' (Existential Subject)**
│   │   │       │   │           ├── **Definition:** 'There' introducing existence
│   │   │       │   │           ├── **Structure:** There + BE + NP (+ location)
│   │   │       │   │           ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │           │   ├── "**There** is a book on the table."
│   │   │       │   │           │   ├── "**There** are many problems."
│   │   │       │   │           │   └── "**There** seems to be an error."
│   │   │       │   │           ├── **Agreement:** Verb agrees with post-verbal NP
│   │   │       │   │           │   └── "There **is** a cat." / "There **are** cats."
│   │   │       │   │           └── **Logical Subject:** Post-verbal NP is the real subject
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   ├── **C. Types of Subject (By Function)**
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(1) Grammatical Subject**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** The NP that agrees with the verb
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Position:** Before finite verb in declaratives
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**The book** was read." (grammatical S = the book)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**It** is raining." (grammatical S = it)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "**There** are problems." (grammatical S = there)
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Test:** Determines verb agreement
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(2) Logical Subject (Semantic Subject)**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** The entity performing action (Agent)
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **May differ from grammatical subject:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── Passive: "The book was read **by her**." (her = logical S)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── Existential: "There is **a book**." (a book = logical S)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── Extraposed: "It is easy **to learn**." (to learn = logical S)
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Test:** Ask "Who/What performs the action?"
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(3) Raised Subject**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Subject moved from lower clause
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Raising Verbs:** seem, appear, tend, happen, be likely
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**She** seems to understand." ← from "It seems [she understands]"
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "**He** appears to be tired." ← from "It appears [he is tired]"
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "**They** are likely to win." ← from "It is likely [they will win]"
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Test:** Subject not a semantic argument of main verb
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   └── **(4) Controlled Subject (PRO)**
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **Definition:** Understood subject of infinitive clause
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **Control Types:**
│   │   │       │   │       │   ├── **Subject Control:** "She₁ wants [PRO₁ to leave]." (PRO = she)
│   │   │       │   │       │   └── **Object Control:** "She asked him₁ [PRO₁ to leave]." (PRO = him)
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │       │   ├── "I₁ promised [PRO₁ to help]." (I controls PRO)
│   │   │       │   │       │   └── "I persuaded her₁ [PRO₁ to go]." (her controls PRO)
│   │   │       │   │       └── **PRO:** Silent pronoun understood from context
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   ├── **D. Thematic Roles of Subject (Semantic)**
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(1) Agent** - Performs action intentionally
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── "**John** broke the window." (John = agent)
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(2) Experiencer** - Experiences state/emotion
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── "**She** feels sad." / "**I** love music."
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(3) Theme/Patient** - Undergoes action/change
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── "**The window** broke." / "**The ice** melted."
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(4) Instrument** - Tool/Means of action
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── "**The key** opened the door." / "**This knife** cuts well."
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(5) Location** - Place
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── "**The garden** is full of flowers." / "**London** has many museums."
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   └── **(6) Causer** - Causes event (not performing directly)
│   │   │       │   │       └── "**The storm** destroyed the house." / "**His words** hurt her."
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   └── **E. Special Subject Constructions**
│   │   │       │       │
│   │   │       │       ├── **(1) Compound Subject** (Two+ NPs joined)
│   │   │       │       │   ├── "**Tom and Jerry** are friends." (plural agreement)
│   │   │       │       │   ├── "**Either she or I** am wrong." (nearest agreement)
│   │   │       │       │   └── "**Neither rain nor snow** stops the mail."
│   │   │       │       │
│   │   │       │       ├── **(2) Postponed Subject** (After verb)
│   │   │       │       │   ├── Existential: "There came **a stranger**." (stranger = postponed S)
│   │   │       │       │   ├── Presentational: "In came **the clown**."
│   │   │       │       │   └── Inversion: "Never have **I** seen such beauty."
│   │   │       │       │
│   │   │       │       ├── **(3) Null Subject (Implied/Pro-drop)**
│   │   │       │       │   ├── **Imperatives:** "[You] Come here!" (you = implied)
│   │   │       │       │   ├── **Diary style:** "[I] Went to the store."
│   │   │       │       │   └── **Note:** English requires overt subjects (unlike Spanish, Italian)
│   │   │       │       │
│   │   │       │       ├── **(4) Heavy Subject Shift** (Extraposition)
│   │   │       │       │   ├── Before: "**That he lied** was obvious."
│   │   │       │       │   ├── After: "**It** was obvious **that he lied**."
│   │   │       │       │   └── Purpose: Avoid heavy subjects in initial position
│   │   │       │       │
│   │   │       │       └── **(5) Subject-Verb Agreement Traps (Exam Focus)**
│   │   │       │           ├── **Intervening phrases:** "The list of items **is** long." (list = S)
│   │   │       │           ├── **Collective nouns:** "The team **is/are** ready." (BrE/AmE differ)
│   │   │       │           ├── **Quantifiers:** "All of the water **is** gone." / "All **are** here."
│   │   │       │           ├── **Inverted:** "There **are** many problems." (problems = real S)
│   │   │       │           └── **Neither/Either:** "Neither he nor they **know**." (nearest)
│   │   │       │
│   │   │       ├── **ii. Predicate**
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   ├── **A. Predicate Types (By Structure)**
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(1) Simple Predicate**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** The main verb or verb phrase alone (no modifiers/objects)
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Structure:** V or Aux + V
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "The cat **sleeps**." (sleeps = simple predicate)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "She **is running**." (is running = simple predicate)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "They **have been waiting**." (have been waiting = simple predicate)
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Identification:** Ask "What is the verb?" - that's the simple predicate
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(2) Compound Predicate**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Two or more verbs/verb phrases sharing the same subject
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Structure:** S + V₁ + (conj.) + V₂ (+ V₃...)
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Connectors:** and, but, or, yet, so, nor
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "She **laughed and cried**." (two actions, one subject)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   ├── "He **ran, jumped, and swam**." (three actions)
│   │   │       │   │   │   │   └── "The dog **barked loudly but wagged its tail**." (contrasting actions)
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Note:** NOT a compound sentence - still one subject
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   └── **(3) Complete Predicate**
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **Definition:** The verb plus ALL modifiers, objects, and complements
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **Structure:** V + (O) + (C) + (M) - everything except subject
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │   │       │   ├── "The cat **sleeps on the warm rug every afternoon**."
│   │   │       │   │       │   │   └── Complete = sleeps + on the warm rug + every afternoon
│   │   │       │   │       │   ├── "She **gave him a beautiful gift yesterday**."
│   │   │       │   │       │   │   └── Complete = gave + him (IO) + gift (DO) + beautiful (mod) + yesterday (adv)
│   │   │       │   │       │   └── "They **elected him president unanimously**."
│   │   │       │   │       │       └── Complete = elected + him (DO) + president (OC) + unanimously (adv)
│   │   │       │   │       └── **Identification:** Remove the subject → everything remaining = complete predicate
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   ├── **B. Predicate Functions (Semantic Roles)**
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(1) Action Predicate** - Describes what subject does
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Transitive:** "She **wrote a letter**." (action + object)
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Intransitive:** "He **ran quickly**." (action, no object)
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Ditransitive:** "She **gave him money**." (action + IO + DO)
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(2) Stative Predicate** - Describes state/condition
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Linking:** "She **is happy**." (state via copula)
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Perception:** "It **seems wrong**." (apparent state)
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Existential:** "There **exists a solution**." (existence state)
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   └── **(3) Resultative Predicate** - Describes resulting state
│   │   │       │   │       ├── "He **hammered the metal flat**." (action → result)
│   │   │       │   │       ├── "She **painted the wall red**." (action → result)
│   │   │       │   │       └── "They **elected him president**." (action → result)
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   ├── **C. Special Predicate Structures**
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(1) Complex Predicate** (Multi-word constructions acting as single predicate)
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Phrasal Verbs:** "She **gave up** smoking." / "He **ran into** trouble."
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Light Verb Constructions:** "**take a walk**", "**make a decision**", "**have a look**"
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Serial Verb:** "**Go get** the book." / "**Come help** me."
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(2) Discontinuous Predicate** (Split by intervening elements)
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Particle separation:** "She **turned** the lights **off**."
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Adverb insertion:** "He **quickly ran** away."
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Negation:** "He **does not understand**."
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   └── **(3) Elliptical Predicate** (Predicate is implied/omitted)
│   │   │       │   │       ├── "She can swim, and he **can [swim]** too."
│   │   │       │   │       ├── "I will if you **[will]**."
│   │   │       │   │       └── **Pro-verb 'do':** "She runs faster than he **does**."
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   ├── **D. Predicate Agreement Rules**
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   ├── **(1) Subject-Verb Agreement**
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Singular:** "The cat **runs**." / "She **is** happy."
│   │   │       │   │   │   ├── **Plural:** "The cats **run**." / "They **are** happy."
│   │   │       │   │   │   └── **Compound subjects:** "Tom and Jerry **are** friends."
│   │   │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │   │   └── **(2) Tense Consistency**
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **Sequence of tenses:** Main clause controls subordinate
│   │   │       │   │       ├── **Reported speech:** "He said he **was** tired." (backshift)
│   │   │       │   │       └── **Conditionals:** "If I **were** rich..." (subjunctive)
│   │   │       │   │
│   │   │       │   └── **Elements of Predicates**
│   │   │       │       │
│   │   │       │       ├── **(1) Verb (V)**
│   │   │       │       │   │
│   │   │       │       │   ├── **(a) Category by Function of Verb**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(i) Main Verb (Lexical Verb)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Carries the core meaning; can stand alone
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Types by Transitivity:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Transitive:** Requires object - "She **reads** books."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Intransitive:** No object - "He **sleeps**." / "Birds **fly**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Ditransitive:** Two objects - "She **gave** him a gift."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Ambitransitive:** Both T/I - "She **eats**." / "She **eats** rice."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **Complex Transitive:** Obj + Complement - "They **made** him captain."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Types by Meaning:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Dynamic/Action:** Movement/activity - run, write, eat, build
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Stative:** State/condition - know, believe, own, love
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **Perception:** Senses - see, hear, feel, taste, smell
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Note:** Stative verbs typically don't take progressive (*I am knowing)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(ii) Auxiliary Verb (Helping Verb)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Helps main verb form tenses, moods, voices
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Primary Auxiliaries:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **BE** (am, is, are, was, were, being, been)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   │   ├── Progressive: "She **is** working."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   │   └── Passive: "The book **was** written."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **HAVE** (have, has, had, having)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   │   └── Perfect: "She **has** finished."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **DO** (do, does, did)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │       ├── Emphasis: "I **do** love you."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │       ├── Negation: "She **does** not know."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │       └── Questions: "**Did** you call?"
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **NICE Properties:** (Negation, Inversion, Code, Emphasis)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── **N**egation: Aux + not → "He **is not** coming."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── **I**nversion: Aux moves before S → "**Is** he coming?"
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── **C**ode (ellipsis): "She can, and I **can** too."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       └── **E**mphasis: Stressed aux → "He **IS** coming!"
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(iii) Modal Verb**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Express modality (possibility, necessity, permission)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Core Modals:** (Followed by bare infinitive)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **can/could** - Ability/Possibility: "She **can** swim."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **may/might** - Permission/Possibility: "You **may** leave."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **will/would** - Future/Volition: "I **will** help."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **shall/should** - Obligation/Advice: "You **should** rest."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **must** - Necessity/Obligation: "You **must** go."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Semi-modals (Quasi-modals):**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **have to** - Obligation: "I **have to** leave."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **ought to** - Moral obligation: "You **ought to** apologize."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **need to** - Necessity: "You **need to** study."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **used to** - Past habit: "I **used to** smoke."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **be going to** - Future: "She **is going to** win."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Modal Properties:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── No -s inflection (*He cans)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── No infinitive form (*to must)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── No participle (*musting, *musted)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       └── Cannot combine (*must can)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   └── **(iv) Linking Verb (Copular Verb)**
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Definition:** Links subject to complement (no action)
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Types:**
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── **True Copulas:** BE only - "She **is** a teacher."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── **Resultative:** become, get, grow, turn, go, come, fall
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   │   └── "He **became** famous." / "She **got** angry."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── **Sensory:** look, sound, smell, taste, feel
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   │   └── "It **looks** good." / "This **tastes** delicious."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── **Seeming:** seem, appear
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   │   └── "He **seems** tired." / "She **appears** happy."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   └── **Continuative:** remain, stay, keep
│   │   │       │       │   │       │       └── "He **remained** calm." / "She **stayed** quiet."
│   │   │       │       │   │       └── **Complement Types after Linking Verbs:**
│   │   │       │       │   │           ├── Noun Phrase: "She is **a doctor**."
│   │   │       │       │   │           ├── Adjective Phrase: "She is **very happy**."
│   │   │       │       │   │           └── Prepositional Phrase: "The book is **on the table**."
│   │   │       │       │   │
│   │   │       │       │   ├── **(b) Category by Form of Verb (Morphology)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(i) Base Form (Bare Infinitive)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Dictionary form; no inflection
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Uses:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── After modals: "She can **write**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Imperatives: "**Write** the answer!"
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Subjunctive: "I demand that he **leave**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── After causatives: "Make him **go**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── After perception verbs: "I saw him **run**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Examples:** go, eat, write, be, have
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(ii) -s Form (3rd Person Singular Present)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Present tense with 3rd person singular subject
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Formation Rules:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Most verbs: + s → runs, eats, writes
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── -ch, -sh, -ss, -x, -o: + es → watches, washes, goes
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── Consonant + y: y → ies → carries, studies
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Irregular:** has (have), does (do), is (be)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Agreement:** "He **runs**." / "She **writes**." / "It **seems**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(iii) -ing Form (Present Participle / Gerund)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** V + -ing
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Formation Rules:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Most verbs: + ing → going, eating
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Silent -e: drop e + ing → writing, taking
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── CVC pattern: double final C → running, swimming
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── -ie: ie → y + ing → lying, dying
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Functions:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Present Participle:** "She is **running**." (progressive)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Gerund (Verbal Noun):** "**Running** is healthy." (subject)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Adjectival:** "The **running** water." (modifier)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **Adverbial:** "**Running** fast, he escaped." (participle clause)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Key Distinction:** Gerund = noun function; Participle = verb/adj function
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(iv) -ed/-en Form (Past / Past Participle)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Past tense and perfect/passive forms
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Regular Formation:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Most verbs: + ed → walked, played
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── -e ending: + d → loved, danced
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── CVC: double C + ed → stopped, planned
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── Consonant + y: y → ied → carried, studied
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Irregular Forms:** (Past ≠ Past Participle in some)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **ABB:** buy-bought-bought, think-thought-thought
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **ABC:** go-went-gone, write-wrote-written
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **AAA:** cut-cut-cut, put-put-put
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **ABA:** come-came-come, run-ran-run
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Functions:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── **Past Tense:** "She **walked** home."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── **Perfect:** "She has **written** a book."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── **Passive:** "The book was **written** by her."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       └── **Adjectival:** "The **broken** window." (modifier)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   └── **(v) Infinitive Form (to + Base)**
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Definition:** 'to' + base form (non-finite)
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Uses:**
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── **Subject:** "**To err** is human."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── **Object:** "She wants **to leave**."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── **Complement:** "His goal is **to win**."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── **Adverbial (purpose):** "He came **to see** her."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   └── **Adjectival:** "A book **to read**."
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Split Infinitive:** to + adv + verb
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── "To **boldly** go..." (acceptable in modern usage)
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   └── Traditional: avoid splitting; Modern: acceptable
│   │   │       │       │   │       └── **Bare vs. Full Infinitive:**
│   │   │       │       │   │           ├── Full: "She wants **to go**."
│   │   │       │       │   │           └── Bare: "She can **go**." (no 'to')
│   │   │       │       │   │
│   │   │       │       │   └── **(c) Category by Type of Verb (Finiteness)**
│   │   │       │       │       │
│   │   │       │       │       ├── **(i) Finite Verb**
│   │   │       │       │       │   ├── **Definition:** Marked for tense and subject agreement
│   │   │       │       │       │   ├── **Properties:**
│   │   │       │       │       │   │   ├── Carries tense: past/present (not modality alone)
│   │   │       │       │       │   │   ├── Shows agreement: I am / He is / They are
│   │   │       │       │       │   │   └── Can be the only verb in independent clause
│   │   │       │       │       │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │       │       │   │   ├── "She **writes** daily." (present, 3rd sg)
│   │   │       │       │       │   │   ├── "They **went** home." (past)
│   │   │       │       │       │   │   └── "He **is** happy." (present, copula)
│   │   │       │       │       │   └── **Key Test:** Can stand as main verb of independent clause
│   │   │       │       │       │
│   │   │       │       │       └── **(ii) Non-finite Verb**
│   │   │       │       │           ├── **Definition:** NOT marked for tense/agreement
│   │   │       │       │           ├── **Types:**
│   │   │       │       │           │   ├── **Infinitive:** to + base → "**To win** is everything."
│   │   │       │       │           │   ├── **Bare Infinitive:** base alone → "Let him **go**."
│   │   │       │       │           │   ├── **Gerund (-ing as noun):** "**Swimming** is fun."
│   │   │       │       │           │   ├── **Present Participle (-ing as modifier):** "The **running** man."
│   │   │       │       │           │   └── **Past Participle (-ed/-en):** "The **broken** vase."
│   │   │       │       │           ├── **Properties:**
│   │   │       │       │           │   ├── Cannot stand alone as main verb (*To go.)
│   │   │       │       │           │   ├── No tense marking (derive tense from context)
│   │   │       │       │           │   └── No subject agreement (*to goes)
│   │   │       │       │           └── **In Clauses:**
│   │   │       │       │               ├── Non-finite clause: "**Having finished**, she left."
│   │   │       │       │               └── As complement: "She wants **to leave**."
│   │   │       │       │
│   │   │       │       ├── **(2) Object (O)**
│   │   │       │       │   │
│   │   │       │       │   ├── **(a) Functions of Object (Syntactic Roles)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(i) Direct Object (DO)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Entity directly affected by verb action
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Identification Test:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Ask "WHAT/WHOM?" after verb
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── Can become subject in passive: "The book was read."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "She read **the book**." (What did she read?)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "He hit **the ball**." (What did he hit?)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── "I saw **him**." (Whom did I see?)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Transitive Verbs requiring DO:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       └── read, write, eat, buy, make, see, hear, love, hate, want, need
