│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(ii) Indirect Object (IO)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Recipient/beneficiary of action (typically person)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Identification Test:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Ask "TO WHOM/FOR WHOM?" after verb
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── Can be replaced by to/for + NP
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Position:** Between verb and DO, or after DO with to/for
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "She gave **him** a book." = "She gave a book **to him**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "I bought **her** flowers." = "I bought flowers **for her**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── "He told **me** the truth." (To whom did he tell?)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Ditransitive Verbs requiring IO + DO:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── **TO-verbs:** give, send, tell, show, teach, offer, lend, bring, pass
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       └── **FOR-verbs:** buy, make, cook, find, save, get
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(iii) Prepositional Object (PO)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** NP/Pronoun governed by a preposition
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Types:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Object of preposition:** "She looked at **him**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **Prepositional verb object:** "I rely on **her**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "He talked about **the project**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "She listened to **the music**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── "They waited for **the bus**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Obligatory Prepositional Objects:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       └── rely on, depend on, consist of, look after, care for, wait for
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(iv) Cognate Object**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Definition:** Object semantically related to (derived from) verb
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "She **dreamed** a **dream**." (dream = cognate)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "He **smiled** a **smile**." (smile = cognate)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "They **lived** a good **life**." (life = cognate)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── "She **sang** a beautiful **song**." (song = cognate)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Note:** Typically used with intransitive verbs
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   └── **(v) Retained Object**
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Definition:** DO that remains in passive of ditransitive
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── Active: "She gave him **a book**."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── Passive: "He was given **a book**." (book = retained DO)
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   └── "They were told **the truth**."
│   │   │       │       │   │       └── **Note:** IO becomes subject; DO is "retained"
│   │   │       │       │   │
│   │   │       │       │   ├── **(b) Forms of Object (Structural Types)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(i) Noun Phrase Object**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Structure:** (Det) + (Adj*) + N + (PP/RC)*
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Simple: "I read **the book**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Complex: "I read **the interesting book on the table**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── Heavy: "I read **the book that you recommended last week**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Heavy NP Shift:** Move complex NP to end
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       └── "She gave **to him** the book that..."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(ii) Pronoun Object**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Case:** Must be OBJECTIVE (me, him, her, us, them, whom)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Types:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Personal:** "I saw **him**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Demonstrative:** "I want **this**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Indefinite:** "I ate **something**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── **Reflexive:** "He hurt **himself**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **Reciprocal:** "They love **each other**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Common Error:** ✘ "between you and I" → ✔ "between you and me"
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(iii) Clausal Object (Finite)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **That-Clause:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "I know **that she is coming**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "He believes **that it's true**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── That-deletion: "I think **(that)** she left."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Wh-Clause (Embedded question):**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "I wonder **what he wants**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "Do you know **where she lives**?"
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── "Ask him **why he did it**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Verbs taking clausal objects:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       └── know, believe, think, wonder, ask, tell, say, realize, hope
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   ├── **(iv) Clausal Object (Non-finite)**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Infinitive Object (to + V):**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "She wants **to leave**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "I hope **to see you**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── **With Object:** "I want **him to go**." (him = subject of inf)
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Gerund Object (-ing):**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "She enjoys **swimming**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── "He avoided **answering**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── "I don't mind **waiting**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   ├── **Infinitive vs. Gerund:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Some verbs take only infinitive: want, hope, decide, promise
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   ├── Some take only gerund: enjoy, avoid, finish, suggest
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   │   └── Some take both (with meaning change): stop, remember, try
│   │   │       │       │   │   │   └── **Bare Infinitive:**
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       ├── After causatives: "Make him **go**." / "Let her **stay**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │       └── After perception: "I saw him **run**."
│   │   │       │       │   │   │
│   │   │       │       │   │   └── **(v) Preparatory/Dummy Object (Anticipatory 'it')**
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Definition:** 'it' holding place for heavy clausal object
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Structure:** V + it + (Adj) + to-inf/that-clause
│   │   │       │       │   │       ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── "I find **it** difficult **to understand**."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   ├── "She makes **it** clear **that she's leaving**."
│   │   │       │       │   │       │   └── "He considers **it** wrong **to lie**."
│   │   │       │       │   │       └── **Verbs with anticipatory 'it':**
│   │   │       │       │   │           └── find, make, consider, think, believe + it + Adj + clause
│   │   │       │       │   │
│   │   │       │       │   └── **(c) Special Object Constructions**
│   │   │       │       │       │
│   │   │       │       │       ├── **(i) Reflexive Object** (Object = Subject)
│   │   │       │       │       │   ├── "She hurt **herself**."
│   │   │       │       │       │   ├── "They blame **themselves**."
│   │   │       │       │       │   └── Pronouns: myself, yourself, himself, herself, itself, ourselves, themselves
│   │   │       │       │       │
│   │   │       │       │       ├── **(ii) Reciprocal Object** (Mutual action)
│   │   │       │       │       │   ├── "They love **each other**."
│   │   │       │       │       │   ├── "We help **one another**."
│   │   │       │       │       │   └── Requires plural/compound subject
│   │   │       │       │       │
│   │   │       │       │       └── **(iii) Object Control** (Object controls infinitive subject)
│   │   │       │       │           ├── "I want **him** to leave." (him = agent of leave)
│   │   │       │       │           ├── "She persuaded **me** to stay." (me = agent of stay)
│   │   │       │       │           └── Control verbs: want, persuade, tell, ask, advise, expect
│   │   │       │       │
│   │   │       │       └── **(3) Complement (C)**
│   │   │       │           │
│   │   │       │           ├── **(a) Functions of Complement (Syntactic Roles)**
│   │   │       │           │   │
│   │   │       │           │   ├── **(i) Subject Complement (SC)**
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Definition:** Describes/renames subject after linking verb
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Structure:** S + Linking V + SC
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Types:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── **Predicative Nominative:** "She is **a doctor**." (NP = subject)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── **Predicative Adjective:** "She is **happy**." (Adj describes subject)
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "The sky looks **blue**." (blue describes sky)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "He became **president**." (president = he)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── "The soup tastes **delicious**." (delicious describes soup)
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Linking Verbs taking SC:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── be, become, seem, appear, look, smell, taste, feel, sound, remain, stay
│   │   │       │           │   │   └── **Case Note:** Formal: "It is **I**." / Informal: "It's **me**."
│   │   │       │           │   │
│   │   │       │           │   ├── **(ii) Object Complement (OC)**
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Definition:** Describes/renames direct object
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Structure:** S + V + DO + OC
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Types:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── **Nominal OC:** "They elected him **president**." (president = him)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── **Adjectival OC:** "She painted it **red**." (red describes it)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── **Infinitive OC:** "I want you **to go**."
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── **Participle OC:** "He kept me **waiting**."
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "We consider him **honest**." (honest = OC)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "They named their daughter **Maria**." (Maria = OC)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── "He drove her **crazy**." (crazy = OC)
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Verbs taking OC:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── **Naming:** call, name, elect, appoint, make, crown
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── **Opinion:** consider, believe, find, think, judge
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── **Causative:** make, drive, keep, leave, get
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── **Resultative:** paint, color, dye, cut
│   │   │       │           │   │   └── **Test:** Replace DO + OC with "as": "consider him honest" = "consider him as honest"
│   │   │       │           │   │
│   │   │       │           │   ├── **(iii) Verb Complement (VC)**
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Definition:** Element required by verb to complete meaning
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Difference from Object:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── Objects are arguments (affected entities)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── Complements complete verb meaning (obligatory elements)
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "He seems **tired**." (Complement, not object)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "She put the book **on the table**." (Locative complement)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── "The meeting lasted **two hours**." (Measure complement)
│   │   │       │           │   │   └── **Obligatory complements:**
│   │   │       │           │   │       └── put (requires location), treat (requires manner), consider (requires evaluation)
│   │   │       │           │   │
│   │   │       │           │   └── **(iv) Prepositional Complement (PC)**
│   │   │       │           │       ├── **Definition:** Completes meaning of preposition
│   │   │       │           │       ├── **Examples:**
│   │   │       │           │       │   ├── "She is afraid **of spiders**." (of spiders = PC to afraid)
│   │   │       │           │       │   ├── "He went **into the house**." (house = complement of into)
│   │   │       │           │       │   └── "I'm interested **in grammar**." (grammar = complement of in)
│   │   │       │           │       └── **Note:** All prepositions require complements (though may be implied)
│   │   │       │           │
│   │   │       │           ├── **(b) Types of Complement (By Structure)**
│   │   │       │           │   │
│   │   │       │           │   ├── **(i) Predicative Complement** (After linking verb)
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Nominal Predicative:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "She is **a teacher**." (NP complement)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "He became **a doctor**." (NP complement)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── **Referential:** Subject and complement refer to same entity
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Adjectival Predicative:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "She is **happy**." (Adj complement)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "The news sounds **alarming**." (Adj complement)
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── **Descriptive:** Describes property of subject
│   │   │       │           │   │   └── **Prepositional Predicative:**
│   │   │       │           │   │       ├── "The book is **on the table**." (PP complement)
│   │   │       │           │   │       └── "He seems **in trouble**." (PP complement)
│   │   │       │           │   │
│   │   │       │           │   ├── **(ii) Objective Complement** (After DO)
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Nominal:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "They elected him **president**."
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── "He called her **a genius**."
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Adjectival:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "She painted the wall **red**."
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── "The news made him **happy**."
│   │   │       │           │   │   ├── **Infinitive:**
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   ├── "I want you **to leave**."
│   │   │       │           │   │   │   └── "She asked him **to help**."
│   │   │       │           │   │   └── **Participle:**
│   │   │       │           │   │       ├── "I heard her **singing**." (-ing)
│   │   │       │           │   │       └── "He found the door **locked**." (-ed)
│   │   │       │           │   │
│   │   │       │           │   └── **(iii) Clausal Complement** (Clause as complement)
│   │   │       │           │       ├── **That-Clause:**
│   │   │       │           │       │   ├── "The fact is **that he lied**."
│   │   │       │           │       │   └── "My hope is **that she will come**."
│   │   │       │           │       ├── **Wh-Clause:**
│   │   │       │           │       │   ├── "The question is **where to go**."
│   │   │       │           │       │   └── "The issue is **what we should do**."
│   │   │       │           │       └── **Infinitive Clause:**
│   │   │       │           │           ├── "Her goal is **to win**."
│   │   │       │           │           └── "My plan is **to leave early**."
│   │   │       │           │
│   │   │       │           └── **(c) Forms/Elements of Complement**
│   │   │       │               │
│   │   │       │               ├── **(i) Noun Phrase / Noun Clause**
│   │   │       │               │   ├── "She is **a brilliant scientist**." (NP)
│   │   │       │               │   └── "The problem is **that he lies constantly**." (N-clause)
│   │   │       │               │
│   │   │       │               ├── **(ii) Pronoun**
│   │   │       │               │   ├── **Formal:** "It is **I**." / "This is **he**."
│   │   │       │               │   └── **Informal:** "It's **me**." / "This is **him**."
│   │   │       │               │
│   │   │       │               ├── **(iii) Adjective Phrase**
│   │   │       │               │   ├── "She seems **very happy**." (AdjP)
│   │   │       │               │   ├── "He appears **quite tired**." (AdjP)
│   │   │       │               │   └── "The coffee tastes **extremely bitter**." (AdjP)
│   │   │       │               │
│   │   │       │               ├── **(iv) Prepositional Phrase**
│   │   │       │               │   ├── "He is **in the garden**." (location)
│   │   │       │               │   ├── "She seems **out of sorts**." (state)
│   │   │       │               │   └── "The book is **on the shelf**." (location)
│   │   │       │               │
│   │   │       │               ├── **(v) Gerund Phrase / Clause**
│   │   │       │               │   ├── "His hobby is **collecting stamps**."
│   │   │       │               │   └── "The problem is **getting there on time**."
│   │   │       │               │
│   │   │       │               ├── **(vi) Infinitive Phrase / Clause**
│   │   │       │               │   ├── "Her goal is **to become president**."
│   │   │       │               │   └── "The plan is **to leave at dawn**."
│   │   │       │               │
│   │   │       │               └── **(vii) That-Clause / Finite Clause**
│   │   │       │                   ├── "The truth is **that he knew all along**."
│   │   │       │                   └── "My belief is **that we will succeed**."
│   │   │       │
│   │   │       └── **iii. Modifiers (M)**
│   │   │           │
│   │   │           ├── **A. Functions of Modifiers (Position-based)**
│   │   │           │   │
│   │   │           │   ├── **(1) Pre-Modifiers (Prenominal Modifiers)**
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(a) Determiners**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Definite Article:** "**the** book"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Indefinite Article:** "**a** book", "**an** apple"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Demonstratives:** "**this** book", "**that** pen"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Possessives:** "**my** book", "**her** pen"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Relative Determiners:** "**which** book", "**whose** pen"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(b) Adjectives**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Simple Adjectives:** "**big** house", "**red** car"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Comparative Adjectives:** "**bigger** house"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Superlative Adjectives:** "**biggest** house"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Compound Adjectives:** "**well-known** author", "**blue-eyed** girl"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Adjective Phrases (with modifiers):** "**very beautiful** garden"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(c) Nouns (Attributive/Noun Adjuncts)**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Simple Noun Adjuncts:** "**stone** wall", "**car** door"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Compound Noun Adjuncts:** "**school** **bus** stop"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Plural Noun Adjuncts:** "**savings** account"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Gerund as Adjunct:** "**sleeping** area"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(d) Participles**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Present Participles:** "**running** water", "**flowing** river"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Past Participles:** "**broken** glass", "**finished** product"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Complex Participles:** "**carefully broken** glass"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(e) Quantifiers**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Definite Quantifiers:** "**all** books", "**most** students"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Indefinite Quantifiers:** "**some** books", "**few** students"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Existential Quantifiers:** "**no** books", "**many** apples"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Universal Quantifiers:** "**every** book", "**each** student"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(f) Numerals**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Cardinal Numerals:** "**three** books", "**twenty-five** students"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Ordinal Numerals:** "**first** place", "**fifth** edition"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Fractional Numerals:** "**half** loaf", "**two-thirds** cup"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Multiplicative Numerals:** "**double** portion", "**triple** threat"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   └── **(g) Degree Modifiers (Intensifiers/Diminishers)**
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **Amplifiers:** "**very** beautiful", "**extremely** cold"
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **Downtoners:** "**quite** nice", "**rather** small"
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **Approximators:** "**almost** perfect", "**nearly** complete"
│   │   │           │   │       └── **Emphasizers:** "**absolutely** stunning", "**completely** wrong"
│   │   │           │   │
│   │   │           │   └── **(2) Post-Modifiers (Postnominal Modifiers)**
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(a) Prepositional Phrases**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Simple PP:** "the book **on the table**", "a woman **in red**"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Complex PP:** "the book **on the table in the corner**"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **PP with gerund:** "the fear **of flying**"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **PP with infinitive:** "the right **to speak**"
│   │   │           │       │   └── **PP with noun clause:** "the idea **of what to do**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(b) Infinitive Phrases/Clauses**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Simple Infinitive:** "something **to eat**"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Complex Infinitive:** "the ability **to learn quickly**"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Infinitive with object:** "desire **to win the trophy**"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Infinitive with complement:** "something **to be proud of**"
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Perfect Infinitive:** "the privilege **to have lived there**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(c) Relative Clauses**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Restrictive (Essential):** "the book **that I bought**"
│   │   │           │       │   │   ├── **Subject relative:** "the man **who left**"
│   │   │           │       │   │   ├── **Object relative:** "the book **which I read**"
│   │   │           │       │   │   ├── **Genitive relative:** "the girl **whose mother is a doctor**"
│   │   │           │       │   │   └── **Adverbial relative:** "the place **where we met**"
│   │   │           │       │   │
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Non-restrictive (Non-essential):** "the book, **which I bought last week**, is excellent"
│   │   │           │       │       ├── **Defining:** "Mary, **who is my friend**"
│   │   │           │       │       ├── **Non-defining:** "Tokyo, **which is the capital**"
│   │   │           │       │       └── **Continuative:** "He left, **which surprised everyone**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(d) Participle Phrases**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Present Participle Phrases:** "the man **standing in the corner**"
│   │   │           │       │   │   ├── **Active voice:** "the girl **singing a song**"
│   │   │           │       │   │   ├── **With time modifier:** "the student **studying for hours**"
│   │   │           │       │   │   └── **Complex:** "the child **running through the park happily**"
│   │   │           │       │   │
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Past Participle Phrases:** "the book **written by Austen**"
│   │   │           │       │   │   ├── **Passive voice:** "the window **broken by the storm**"
│   │   │           │       │   │   ├── **Simple:** "the destroyed city"
│   │   │           │       │   │   └── **Complex:** "the house **built in 1890**"
│   │   │           │       │   │
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Perfect Participle Phrases:** "the guest **having arrived late**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(e) Gerund Phrases**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Simple Gerund:** "the art **of cooking**"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Gerund with object:** "the fear **of falling**"
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Complex Gerund:** "the difficulty **in understanding complex theories**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(f) Noun Clauses**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Relative noun clauses:** "the way **that she solved it**"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Interrogative noun clauses:** "the question **whether he'll come**"
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Appositives:** "the idea **that education matters**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(g) Adjectival Clauses (Finite)**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **With be-verb:** "a person **who is trustworthy**"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **With modal:** "something **that might help**"
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Reduced:** "a student **capable of excellence**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       └── **(h) Appositives**
│   │   │           │           ├── **Noun appositives:** "My friend, **a teacher**"
│   │   │           │           ├── **Phrase appositives:** "His job, **teaching English**"
│   │   │           │           └── **Clause appositives:** "The fact **that he won**"
│   │   │           │
│   │   │           ├── **B. Types of Modifiers (Form-based)**
│   │   │           │   │
│   │   │           │   ├── **(1) Adjectival Modifiers (Modify Nouns/Pronouns/NPs)**
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(a) Single Adjectives**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Descriptive Adjectives:** "a **beautiful** painting", "a **tall** building"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Demonstrative Adjectives:** "**this** book", "**that** girl"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Possessive Adjectives:** "**my** pen", "**their** house"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Interrogative Adjectives:** "**which** way", "**what** time"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Quantifier Adjectives:** "**several** students", "**much** effort"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Number Adjectives:** "**three** books", "**tenth** place"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Quality Adjectives:** "**happy** children", "**intelligent** teacher"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Color Adjectives:** "**blue** sky", "**red** rose"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Age Adjectives:** "**old** house", "**young** man"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Size Adjectives:** "**small** dog", "**huge** elephant"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Material Adjectives:** "**wooden** door", "**silk** scarf"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Origin Adjectives:** "**French** wine", "**Indian** food"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(b) Adjective Phrases**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Intensified adjectives:** "**very beautiful** painting", "**extremely cold** weather"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Comparative phrases:** "**more beautiful** than expected", "**as tall as** his brother"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Adjective + PP:** "**aware of** the problem", "**worthy of** praise"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Adjective + infinitive:** "**ready to** go", "**difficult to** understand"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Coordinated adjectives:** "**beautiful and intelligent** woman"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Complex AP:** "**noticeably more beautiful** painting"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(c) Participles as Adjectival Modifiers**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Present Participles:** "**laughing** children", "**sleeping** puppy"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **With adverb:** "**quickly running** horse"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   └── **Reduced relative:** "the student **working on the project**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Past Participles:** "**broken** glass", "**finished** product"
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **With adverb:** "**carefully broken** vase"
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **Passive reduced:** "the car **damaged in the accident**"
│   │   │           │   │   │       └── **Adjectivized participle:** "**married** man", "**scared** child"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(d) Nouns as Adjectival Modifiers (Attributive Nouns/Noun Adjuncts)**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Singular noun adjuncts:** "**stone** wall", "**coffee** cup"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Plural noun adjuncts:** "**savings** account", "**customs** office"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Compound noun adjuncts:** "**basketball** **court**, **school** **bus** stop"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Proper nouns as adjuncts:** "**Shakespeare** **plays**, **Christmas** **dinner**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Noun chains:** "**language** **teacher** **training** **program**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Non-count noun adjuncts:** "**milk** container", "**furniture** store"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(e) Genitives and Possessives as Adjectival Modifiers**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Possessive pronouns:** "**my** book", "**their** house", "**whose** pen"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Possessive noun phrases:** "**John's** car", "**the teacher's** desk"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Double genitive:** "a friend **of John's**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Genitive with 's:** "**Mary's** **beautiful** dress"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Genitive with of:** "the book **of the girl**"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(f) Prepositional Phrases as Adjectival Modifiers**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **PP with different prepositions:** "book **on the shelf**", "girl **in red**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Complex PP:** "the man **in the corner of the room**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **PP with temporal meaning:** "the person **of our time**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **PP chains:** "**of the house** **in the city** **near the river**"
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   └── **(g) Relative Clauses as Adjectival Modifiers**
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **Defining/Restrictive:** "the book **that I bought**"
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **Non-defining/Non-restrictive:** "Shakespeare, **who was born in 1564**"
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **Reduced relative clauses:** "the man **standing there**"
│   │   │           │   │       └── **Finite relative:** "the student **who passed the exam**"
│   │   │           │   │
│   │   │           │   ├── **(2) Adverbial Modifiers (Modify Verbs, Adjectives, Adverbs, or Sentences)**
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(a) Forms of Adverbial Modifiers**
│   │   │           │   │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **(i) Single Adverbs**
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Manner adverbs:** "**quickly**", "**beautifully**", "**carefully**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Time adverbs:** "**yesterday**", "**soon**", "**always**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Place adverbs:** "**here**", "**upstairs**", "**outside**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Frequency adverbs:** "**often**", "**rarely**", "**never**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Degree adverbs:** "**very**", "**quite**", "**extremely**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Aspect adverbs:** "**still**", "**already**", "**yet**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Sentence adverbs:** "**Clearly**", "**Frankly**", "**Fortunately**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   └── **Focuser adverbs:** "**only**", "**even**", "**also**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **(ii) Adverb Phrases**
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Intensified adverbs:** "**very carefully**", "**quite well**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Adverb + PP:** "**in a hurry**", "**with care**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Comparative adverbs:** "**more slowly** than before"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   └── **Complex adverb phrases:** "**much more carefully** than expected"
│   │   │           │   │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **(iii) Prepositional Phrases as Adverbials**
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Manner PP:** "She wrote **with elegance**."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Time PP:** "They arrived **in the morning**."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Place PP:** "He sat **in the corner**."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Cause/Reason PP:** "He trembled **with fear**."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Accompanying PP:** "She walked **with her friend**."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Means PP:** "We communicate **by email**."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   └── **Instrument PP:** "He cut it **with a knife**."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **(iv) Infinitive Phrases as Adverbials**
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Purpose infinitives:** "I came **to help**."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Result infinitives:** "He's too weak **to lift it**."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Reason infinitives:** "**To be honest**, I don't agree."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   └── **Condition infinitives:** "**To hear him tell it**, he's a hero."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **(v) Non-finite Clauses as Adverbials (Participle Clauses)**
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Present participle clauses:** "**Walking in the park**, she saw her friend."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Past participle clauses:** "**Finished with work**, he went home."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Perfect participle clauses:** "**Having completed the task**, they left."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   ├── **Absolute phrases:** "**The work being done**, we left."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │   └── **Complex non-finite:** "**Arriving at the station quickly**, they caught the train."
│   │   │           │   │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **(vi) Finite Clauses as Adverbials (Subordinate Clauses)**
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **Temporal clauses:** "**When she arrived**, everyone cheered."
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **Conditional clauses:** "**If you practice**, you'll improve."
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **Causal clauses:** "**Because he was tired**, he left early."
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **Concessive clauses:** "**Although she studied**, she failed."
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **Purpose clauses:** "I did it **so that she would understand**."
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **Result clauses:** "He ran so fast **that he got tired**."
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **Manner clauses:** "She behaved **as though nothing happened**."
│   │   │           │   │   │       ├── **Comparison clauses:** "He works harder **than she does**."
│   │   │           │   │   │       └── **Place clauses:** "I'll go **wherever you go**."
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   └── **(b) Semantic Functions of Adverbial Modifiers (Meaning-based)**
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(i) Manner (How? / In what way?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Definition:** Describes how an action is performed
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Examples:** "She **spoke softly**." / "He ran **frantically**."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **With adverbs:** "**quickly**", "**carefully**", "**elegantly**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **With PP:** "**with care**", "**in a whisper**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **With participles:** "**walking slowly**, she approached"
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **Position:** Usually after verb or at end of clause
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(ii) Place (Where? / In what location?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Definition:** Indicates where an action occurs
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Examples:** "He lives **in the city**." / "They met **near the station**."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Adverbs:** "**here**", "**there**", "**upstairs**", "**outside**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **PP:** "**at home**", "**in the corner**", "**under the bridge**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Direction PP:** "**to the market**", "**from school**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **With spatial relationships:** "**above the table**", "**between the trees**"
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(iii) Time (When? / How long?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **When (Point in time):**
│   │   │           │   │       │   │   ├── **Adverbs:** "**today**", "**yesterday**", "**now**", "**then**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   │   ├── **PP:** "**at noon**", "**in the morning**", "**on Monday**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   │   └── **Clauses:** "**when she arrived**", "**as he spoke**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   │
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Duration (How long):**
│   │   │           │   │       │   │   ├── **PP:** "**for three hours**", "**throughout the day**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   │   ├── **Adverbs:** "**long**", "**briefly**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   │   └── **Expressions:** "**all night**", "**the whole week**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   │
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **Sequence (In what order):**
│   │   │           │   │       │       ├── "**First**, we ate." / "**Then**, we played."
│   │   │           │   │       │       ├── "**Later**, he arrived." / "**Finally**, we left."
│   │   │           │   │       │       └── "**Meanwhile**, others waited."
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(iv) Frequency (How often? / At what intervals?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Definite frequency:** "**every day**", "**once a week**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Indefinite frequency:** "**often**", "**sometimes**", "**rarely**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Absolute frequency:** "**never**", "**always**", "**ever**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Quasi-frequency:** "**almost never**", "**hardly ever**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **Common adverbs:** "usually", "frequently", "occasionally", "seldom"
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(v) Purpose/Goal (Why? / For what reason? / With what intention?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Infinitive phrase:** "I came **to help**." / "She studied **to pass the exam**."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Purpose clause:** "I did this **so that she would understand**."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **PP with purpose:** "**for the purpose of** winning"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Conjunctions:** "**so that**", "**in order that**", "**lest**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **Examples:** "He trained hard **to win the medal**."
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(vi) Reason/Cause (Why? / Because of what?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Causal clauses:** "He left **because he was tired**." / "**Since it rained**, we stayed home."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **PP with cause:** "**out of fear**", "**from exhaustion**", "**due to circumstances**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Participle clause:** "**Seeing the danger**, he ran away."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Conjunctions:** "because", "since", "as", "for"
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **Examples:** "**For this reason**, I disagree."
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(vii) Condition (Under what circumstances? / What must happen?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Conditional clauses:** "**If you practice**, you'll improve."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Real conditions:** "**If it rains**, I'll stay home."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Unreal conditions:** "**If I were rich**, I'd travel."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Mixed conditions:** "**If he had studied**, he would pass."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Conjunctions:** "if", "unless", "provided that", "as long as"
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **Inversion structures:** "**Should you need help**, call me."
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(viii) Concession (Despite what? / What happens even though?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Concessive clauses:** "**Although she studied**, she failed." / "**Even though it was late**, he continued."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Concessive PP:** "**Despite the rain**, we went out."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Conjunctions:** "although", "even though", "though", "while"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Inversion:** "**Much as I wanted to**, I couldn't go."
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **Examples:** "**In spite of his talent**, he failed."
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(ix) Result/Consequence (What happened as a result?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Result clauses:** "He worked so hard **that he got exhausted**."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Conjunctions:** "so", "so...that", "such...that"
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Infinitive phrases:** "He was **too tired to continue**."
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **Examples:** "She was **such an excellent student** that she won awards."
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **(x) Manner/Comparison (In what way? / Like what?)**
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Comparative clauses:** "He works **as hard as** she does."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Manner clauses:** "She behaved **as though nothing happened**."
│   │   │           │   │       │   ├── **Similes:** "white **as snow**", "fast **like lightning**"
│   │   │           │   │       │   └── **Examples:** "She sang **the way her mother taught her**."
│   │   │           │   │       │
│   │   │           │   │       └── **(xi) Degree (To what extent? / How much?)**
│   │   │           │   │           ├── **Intensifiers:** "**very**", "**extremely**", "**incredibly**"
│   │   │           │   │           ├── **Downtoners:** "**quite**", "**rather**", "**somewhat**"
│   │   │           │   │           ├── **Modifying adjectives:** "**very beautiful**", "**quite cold**"
│   │   │           │   │           ├── **Modifying adverbs:** "**very quickly**", "**extremely carefully**"
│   │   │           │   │           └── **Scale expressions:** "**much more**, **a lot less**, **far better**"
│   │   │           │   │
│   │   │           │   ├── **(3) Adverbial Modifiers Modifying Adjectives (Degree Modifiers)**
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(a) Intensifiers (Amplifiers)**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Strong intensifiers:** "**very**", "**extremely**", "**incredibly**", "**terribly**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Moderate intensifiers:** "**quite**", "**fairly**", "**rather**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Booster intensifiers:** "**absolutely**", "**completely**", "**totally**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Examples:** "**very** beautiful", "**extremely** cold", "**totally** amazing"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Position:** Always immediately before the adjective
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(b) Downtoners (Diminishers)**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Modest downtoners:** "**rather**", "**somewhat**", "**kind of**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Approximators:** "**almost**", "**nearly**", "**practically**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Minimal force:** "**barely**", "**scarcely**", "**hardly**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Examples:** "**rather** cold", "**almost** perfect", "**barely** visible"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Semantic effect:** Reduces intensity of adjective
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   ├── **(c) Approximators**
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Near-identity:** "**practically**", "**virtually**", "**essentially**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Partial match:** "**somewhat**", "**rather**", "**fairly**"
│   │   │           │   │   │   ├── **Examples:** "**virtually** impossible", "**practically** perfect"
│   │   │           │   │   │   └── **Function:** Indicates degree of approximation
│   │   │           │   │   │
│   │   │           │   │   └── **(d) Emphasizers**
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **Absolute emphasizers:** "**absolutely**", "**definitely**", "**certainly**"
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **Focus emphasizers:** "**really**", "**truly**", "**genuinely**"
│   │   │           │   │       ├── **Examples:** "**absolutely** beautiful", "**really** important"
│   │   │           │   │       └── **Position:** Before the adjective, sometimes with comma
│   │   │           │   │
│   │   │           │   └── **(4) Nominal Modifiers (Nouns modifying Nouns)**
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(a) Simple Noun Adjuncts**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Common patterns:** "stone wall", "car door", "coffee cup"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Function:** First noun modifies/specifies the head noun
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Semantics:** Material, purpose, location, composition
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Stress pattern:** Primary stress on head noun
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Examples:** "**glass** table", "**brick** building", "**leather** jacket"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(b) Compound Noun Adjuncts**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Two-modifier compounds:** "school bus", "basketball court"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Three-modifier chains:** "school bus stop", "language teacher training"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Hyphenated compounds:** "mother-in-law's house"
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Examples:** "**English** **teacher** **training** **program**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(c) Plural Noun Adjuncts**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Plural form:** "savings account", "customs office", "sports day"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Meaning:** Often indicates classification or domain
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Examples:** "**supplies** **closet**", "**products** **line**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(d) Proper Noun Adjuncts**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Place adjuncts:** "Paris fashion", "French cuisine", "Tokyo sky"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Person adjuncts:** "Shakespeare plays", "Darwin theory"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Time period adjuncts:** "summer vacation", "Monday morning"
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Examples:** "**Christmas** **dinner**", "**Sunday** **school**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       ├── **(e) Gerund as Noun Adjunct**
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Gerund forms:** "sleeping area", "reading room", "walking path"
│   │   │           │       │   ├── **Function:** Describes what occurs in the location
│   │   │           │       │   └── **Examples:** "**cooking** **class**", "**swimming** **pool**", "**waiting** **room**"
│   │   │           │       │
│   │   │           │       └── **(f) Noun Chains and Complex Sequences**
│   │   │           │           ├── **Typical order:** Material + Color + Size + Origin + Noun
│   │   │           │           ├── **Example chains:** "large red Italian marble table"
│   │   │           │           ├── **Left-branching structures:** "government policy decision maker"
│   │   │           │           ├── **Right-branching structures:** "table in the corner near the window"
│   │   │           │           └── **Mixed structures:** "antique **English** **oak** **dining** **room** **furniture**"
│   │   │           │
│   │   │           └── **C. Restrictions and Constraints on Modifiers**
│   │   │               │
│   │   │               ├── **(1) Positional Constraints**
│   │   │               │   ├── **Pre-modifiers only:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── Determiners, quantifiers, numerals, most adjectives
│   │   │               │   │   └── Cannot follow noun (e.g., "*book the*" is wrong)
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   ├── **Post-modifiers only:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── Relative clauses, most participial phrases, infinitives
│   │   │               │   │   └── Cannot precede noun (e.g., "*to read book*" is wrong)
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   ├── **Either pre or post (with different meanings):**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── "an old friend" (pre) vs. "a friend of old" (post, archaic)
│   │   │               │   │   └── "a mere suggestion" (pre) vs. "nothing mere" (post, rare)
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   └── **Position-sensitive modifiers:**
│   │   │               │       ├── Adjectives: "present student" vs. "student present"
│   │   │               │       └── Participles: "running man" vs. "man running"
│   │   │               │
│   │   │               ├── **(2) Ordering Constraints (Adjective Stacking)**
│   │   │               │   ├── **Universal order (Ticknor's order):**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── Opinion → Size → Age → Color → Origin → Material → Noun
│   │   │               │   │   └── Example: "beautiful large old red Italian marble table"
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   ├── **Coordinate vs. cumulative:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── **Coordinate:** Can be reordered (beautiful, comfortable room)
│   │   │               │   │   └── **Cumulative:** Cannot be reordered (*comfortable beautiful room)
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   ├── **Common sequences:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── Demonstrative + Number + Descriptive: "these three beautiful paintings"
│   │   │               │   │   └── Possessive + Number + Descriptive: "my five red roses"
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   └── **Comma rules:**
│   │   │               │       ├── Coordinate adjectives: separated by commas or "and"
│   │   │               │       └── Cumulative adjectives: no commas
│   │   │               │
│   │   │               ├── **(3) Syntactic Compatibility**
│   │   │               │   ├── **Gradability:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── **Gradable adjectives:** "very beautiful", "*very married"
│   │   │               │   │   ├── **Absolute adjectives:** "perfect", "unique", "dead"
│   │   │               │   │   └── Cannot be intensified: "*very perfect", "*quite dead"
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   ├── **Comparability:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── **Comparative forms:** "more beautiful", "taller"
│   │   │               │   │   ├── **Superlative forms:** "most beautiful", "tallest"
│   │   │               │   │   └── **Restriction:** Some adjectives don't allow comparison
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   └── **Predicate restrictions:**
│   │   │               │       ├── Some adjectives only pre-modify: "mere suggestion", "*suggestion is mere"
│   │   │               │       └── Some only post-modify or function as predicates
│   │   │               │
│   │   │               ├── **(4) Semantic Constraints**
│   │   │               │   ├── **Compatibility with head noun:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── "wooden door" (compatible) vs. "*wooden idea" (incompatible)
│   │   │               │   │   ├── "beautiful painting" (compatible) vs. "*beautiful rock" (strange)
│   │   │               │   │   └── Depends on noun semantics and selectional restrictions
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   ├── **Mutually exclusive modifiers:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── "old and new" (contradictory when used together)
│   │   │               │   │   ├── "*big small" (contradictory)
│   │   │               │   │   └── Pragmatic constraints on combination
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   └── **Idiomatic restrictions:**
│   │   │               │       ├── Some combinations are conventionalized
│   │   │               │       └── "black market", "white lie" (transparent meaning)
│   │   │               │
│   │   │               ├── **(5) Morphological Constraints**
│   │   │               │   ├── **Participle agreement:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── Present participles: "running man" (must agree with head)
│   │   │               │   │   └── Past participles: "broken glass" (passive form)
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   ├── **Adjective inflection:**
│   │   │               │   │   ├── Comparative/superlative forms
│   │   │               │   │   ├── Predicative vs. attributive forms
│   │   │               │   │   └── Some adjectives lack certain forms
│   │   │               │   │
│   │   │               │   └── **Genitive formation:**
│   │   │               │       ├── Noun genitive: "John's", "the teacher's"
│   │   │               │       ├── Compound genitive: "the King of Spain's palace"
│   │   │               │       └── Restrictions on pronoun genitives
│   │   │               │
│   │   │               └── **(6) Pragmatic and Discourse Constraints**
│   │   │                   ├── **Given vs. new information:**
│   │   │                   │   ├── Restrictive modifiers introduce new information
│   │   │                   │   └── Non-restrictive modifiers provide added information
│   │   │                   │
│   │   │                   ├── **Information structure:**
│   │   │                   │   ├── Theme (given) typically precedes rheme (new)
│   │   │                   │   └── Modifiers can affect information distribution
│   │   │                   │
│   │   │                   ├── **Register and style:**
│   │   │                   │   ├── Formal vs. informal modifiers
│   │   │                   │   ├── Literary vs. colloquial combinations
│   │   │                   │   └── Domain-specific usage
│   │   │                   │
│   │   │                   └── **Frequency-based constraints:**
│   │   │                       ├── Some modifier combinations are more common than others
│   │   │                       ├── User expectations influence acceptability
│   │   │                       └── Innovative combinations may be striking or awkward
│   │   │
│   │   └── **2. Phrase**
│   │       │
│   │       ├── **A. Definition and Characteristics**
│   │       │   ├── **Definition:** A group of words that function as a single unit but lack a finite verb (or contain one non-finite verb)
│   │       │   ├── **Key features:**
│   │       │   │   ├── Headed structure (contains a head word)
│   │       │   │   ├── Cannot stand alone as a complete sentence
│   │       │   │   ├── Functions as a single grammatical unit
│   │       │   │   ├── May contain modifiers and/or complements
│   │       │   │   └── Part of a larger clause or sentence
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   └── **Structure types:**
│   │       │       ├── **Simple phrases:** Head only (e.g., "books")
│   │       │       ├── **Modified phrases:** Head + modifier (e.g., "red books")
│   │       │       ├── **Complemented phrases:** Head + complement (e.g., "books on the shelf")
│   │       │       └── **Complex phrases:** Head + modifiers + complements (e.g., "very old books on the dusty shelf")
│   │       │
│   │       ├── **B. a. Noun Phrase (NP)**
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(1) Basic Structure**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Minimum NP:** Noun only
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**Books** are useful." / "**She** smiled."
│   │       │   │   │   └── Can be a pronoun: "**I** came." / "**This** works."
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Typical NP:** Determiner + Noun
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**the** book" / "**a** car" / "**my** house"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**this** idea" / "**every** student"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Extended NP:** Determiner + Modifier(s) + Noun + Modifier(s)
│   │       │   │       ├── "**the** **beautiful** **old** **wooden** table"
│   │       │   │       └── "**some** **interesting** books **on the shelf** **that I bought**"
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(2) Constituent Elements**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Determiner (optional but common)**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Definite articles:** "the"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Indefinite articles:** "a", "an"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Demonstratives:** "this", "that", "these", "those"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Possessives:** "my", "your", "his", "her", "our", "their"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Quantifiers:** "some", "many", "few", "all", "no"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Numerals:** "three", "twenty", "first"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Interrogatives:** "which", "what", "whose"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Pre-modifiers (before noun)**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Adjectives:** "**beautiful** house" / "**large** **red** buildings"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Participles:** "**running** water" / "**broken** glass"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Nouns (as modifiers):** "**stone** wall" / "**coffee** cup"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Genitives:** "**John's** car" / "**the teacher's** desk"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Degree modifiers:** "**very** expensive book" / "**quite** interesting"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Head Noun (obligatory)**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Common nouns:** "book", "table", "person", "idea"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Proper nouns:** "Mary", "London", "Shakespeare"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Mass nouns:** "water", "sand", "information"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Count nouns:** "book", "table", "student"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Abstract nouns:** "beauty", "justice", "love"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Post-modifiers (after noun)**
│   │       │   │       ├── **Prepositional phrases:** "book **on the shelf**" / "girl **in red**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Relative clauses:** "person **who came**" / "idea **that worked**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Participial phrases:** "man **standing there**" / "books **written recently**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Infinitive phrases:** "something **to do**" / "ability **to succeed**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Gerund phrases:** "art **of cooking**" / "fear **of flying**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Noun clauses:** "question **whether he'll come**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Appositives:** "**my friend**, **a teacher**"
│   │       │   │       └── **Adjectives (predicative):** "**something** **blue**" (archaic/poetic)
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(3) Types of NPs by Headword**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Pronoun phrases:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Personal pronouns:** "I", "you", "he", "she", "it", "we", "they"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Possessive pronouns:** "mine", "yours", "his", "hers", "ours", "theirs"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Reflexive pronouns:** "myself", "yourself", "himself", "herself"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Demonstrative pronouns:** "this", "that", "these", "those"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Relative pronouns:** "who", "whom", "which", "that", "whose"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Interrogative pronouns:** "who", "what", "which", "whose"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Noun phrases with concrete heads:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**the** **red** **apple** **on the tree**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**several** **old** **wooden** **houses** **near the river**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**John's** **beautiful** **new** **car** **in the garage**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Noun phrases with abstract heads:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**the** **idea** **that he proposed**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**strong** **feeling** **of uncertainty**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**complete** **lack** **of evidence**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Nominalized phrases (gerunds, infinitives):**
│   │       │   │       ├── "**Running** **in the morning** is healthy."
│   │       │   │       ├── "**To understand** **his theory** requires patience."
│   │       │   │       └── "**Completion** **of the project** took three months."
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(4) Functions of NPs in Sentences**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Subject NP:** "**The girl** **in the corner** is my friend."
│   │       │   │   ├── **Object NP:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── Direct object: "I saw **the beautiful sunset**."
│   │       │   │   │   ├── Indirect object: "She gave **me** a book."
│   │       │   │   │   └── Object of preposition: "He talked about **his childhood**."
│   │       │   │   ├── **Complement NP:** "She is **a teacher**."
│   │       │   │   ├── **Appositive NP:** "My brother, **a doctor**, lives here."
│   │       │   │   ├── **Modifier NP (noun adjunct):** "**Stone** wall" / "**Dinner** party"
│   │       │   │   └── **Predicate NP:** "She became **an architect**."
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(5) Complexity and Embedding**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Simple NPs (minimal modification):**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**books**" / "**the** **books**" / "**red** **books**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**my** **beautiful** **car**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Complex NPs (multiple modifiers/complements):**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**the** **large** **old** **red** **brick** **houses** **on** **the** **hill** **that** **I** **saw** **yesterday**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**many** **small** **interesting** **books** **about** **English** **grammar** **in** **the** **library**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Embedded NPs (NPs within NPs):**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "the **book** **of** [**John's** **friend**]"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "the **father** **of** [**the** **girl**]"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Right-branching NPs:**
│   │       │   │       ├── Head + series of post-modifiers
│   │       │   │       └── "the **book** **on the table** **in the corner** **near the window**"
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(6) Special NP Types**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Definite NPs (with clear reference):**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**The** sun" / "**My** house" / "**This** student"
│   │       │   │   │   └── Function: Refer to specific, known entities
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Indefinite NPs (with no clear reference):**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**A** book" / "**Some** apples" / "**Any** student"
│   │       │   │   │   └── Function: Refer to non-specific or unknown entities
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Bare NPs (without determiners):**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**Books** are useful." (generic plural)
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "I like **apples**." (generic plural)
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**Snow** is white." (mass noun)
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Possessive NPs:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**John's** car" / "**the teacher's** desk"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**mine**" / "**yours**" / "**theirs**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**the king's** palace" / "**of John**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Demonstrative NPs:**
│   │       │   │       ├── "**This** is beautiful." / "**That** one is better."
│   │       │   │       ├── "**These** books are mine." / "**Those** students left."
│   │       │   │       └── Can stand alone or modify noun
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   └── **(7) Constraints and Patterns**
│   │       │       ├── **Agreement within NP:**
│   │       │       │   ├── Determiner-noun agreement: "**this** book" (singular) vs. "**these** books" (plural)
│   │       │       │   ├── Adjective-noun agreement: "**beautiful** girl" / "**beautiful** girls"
│   │       │       │   └── Demonstrative-noun agreement: "**this** book" vs. "**that** book"
│   │       │       │
│   │       │       ├── **Ordering of pre-modifiers:**
│   │       │       │   ├── Determiner > Quantifier > Ordinal > Cardinal > Adjective > Noun
│   │       │       │   ├── Example: "**the** **few** **first** **two** **beautiful** **red** **roses**"
│   │       │       │   └── Not all slots must be filled
│   │       │       │
│   │       │       ├── **Adjective coordination:**
│   │       │       │   ├── Coordinate adjectives: "**big, beautiful** house" (commas or "and")
│   │       │       │   ├── Cumulative adjectives: "**dark green** house" (no commas)
│   │       │       │   └── Order matters: "*green dark house" is unacceptable
│   │       │       │
│   │       │       └── **Prosody and stress:**
│   │       │           ├── Primary stress on head noun: "RED books"
│   │       │           ├── Secondary stress on modifiers: "red BOOKS"
│   │       │           └── Can affect meaning: "WHITE house" vs. "white HOUSE"
│   │       │
│   │       ├── **B. b. Verb Phrase (VP)**
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(1) Basic Structure**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Minimum VP:** Verb only (finite or non-finite)
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**Went**." (past tense) / "**Go**." (imperative)
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**Reading** is fun." (gerund)
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**To go** is my wish." (infinitive)
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **VP with complements:** Verb + Object/Complement
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**read** books" / "**gave** her **a gift**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**is** **happy**" / "**became** **a teacher**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Extended VP:** Verb + Complements + Modifiers
│   │       │   │       ├── "**read** **books** **carefully** **in the morning**"
│   │       │   │       └── "**gave** **her** **a gift** **yesterday** **in the garden**"
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(2) Constituent Elements**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Head Verb (obligatory)**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Main/lexical verbs:** "read", "run", "jump", "speak"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Auxiliary verbs:** "be", "have", "do"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Modal verbs:** "can", "will", "must", "should"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Semi-modals:** "ought to", "have to", "used to"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Copulas:** "be", "become", "seem", "appear"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Auxiliary + Main Verb combinations:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Simple:** "**walks**" / "**read**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Perfect:** "**has walked**" / "**have read**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Progressive:** "**is walking**" / "**are reading**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Perfect progressive:** "**has been walking**" / "**have been reading**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Passive:** "**is read**" / "**was given**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Passive perfect:** "**has been read**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Modal + main:** "**can read**" / "**will go**" / "**must understand**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Complements (depend on verb valency)**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Direct object (NP):** "**read** **books**" / "**saw** **them**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Indirect object (NP):** "**gave** **her** **a gift**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Subject complement:** "**is** **a teacher**" / "**seems** **happy**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Object complement:** "**made** **her** **happy**" / "**painted** **it** **blue**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Prepositional complement:** "**depend** **on** **luck**" / "**listen** **to** **music**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Infinitive complement:** "**want** **to** **leave**" / "**help** **carry**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Gerund complement:** "**enjoy** **reading**" / "**avoid** **being seen**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Noun clause complement:** "**know** **that** **he came**" / "**ask** **what** **happened**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **That-clause complement:** "**believe** **that she's right**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Adverbial modifiers (adjuncts)**
│   │       │   │       ├── **Manner:** "**run** **quickly**" / "**spoke** **softly**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Time:** "**left** **yesterday**" / "**came** **in the morning**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Place:** "**lived** **in Paris**" / "**sat** **here**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Frequency:** "**went** **often**" / "**visits** **every day**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Purpose:** "**came** **to help**" / "**studied** **for the exam**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Reason:** "**left** **because she was tired**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Condition:** "**would** **if** **possible**"
│   │       │   │       └── **Concession:** "**went** **despite the rain**"
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(3) Types of VPs by Tense and Aspect**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Simple tenses:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Simple present:** "**reads**" / "**go**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Simple past:** "**read**" / "**went**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Simple future:** "**will read**" / "**will go**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Perfect tenses:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Present perfect:** "**has read**" / "**have gone**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Past perfect:** "**had read**" / "**had gone**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Future perfect:** "**will have read**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Progressive tenses:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Present progressive:** "**is reading**" / "**are going**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Past progressive:** "**was reading**" / "**were going**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Future progressive:** "**will be reading**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Perfect progressive:**
│   │       │   │       ├── **Present perfect progressive:** "**has been reading**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Past perfect progressive:** "**had been reading**"
│   │       │   │       └── **Future perfect progressive:** "**will have been reading**"
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(4) Types of VPs by Voice**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Active voice:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── Agent performs the action: "**read** **books**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**John** **broke** **the** **window**."
│   │       │   │   │   └── Standard, more direct presentation
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Passive voice:**
│   │       │   │       ├── Agent receives the action: "**is read**" / "**be given**"
│   │       │   │       ├── "**The** **window** **was broken** **by** **John**."
│   │       │   │       ├── Emphasizes the action or object
│   │       │   │       └── Agent may be omitted: "**The** **window** **was broken**."
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(5) Types of VPs by Mood**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Indicative:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**She** **speaks** **English**." (assertion)
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**Did** **they** **arrive**?" (question)
│   │       │   │   │   └── Most common mood
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Subjunctive:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "I demand **that she** **be** **here**."
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**If** **he** **were** **here**..." (contrary to fact)
│   │       │   │   │   └── Expresses doubt, wish, condition
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Imperative:**
│   │       │   │       ├── "**Go!**" / "**Close** **the** **door**!"
│   │       │   │       ├── "**Let's** **go**!" (1st person inclusive)
│   │       │   │       └── Gives commands or requests
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(6) Complex VPs with Multiple Auxiliaries**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Modal + have + been + -ing:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**must have been reading**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**could have been watching**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── Complex temporal and aspectual information
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Tense + perfect + progressive:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**will have been reading**" for three hours
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**has been reading**" all morning
│   │       │   │   │   └── Combines multiple temporal dimensions
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Negation in VPs:**
│   │       │   │       ├── "**does** **not** **read**" / "**did** **not** **go**"
│   │       │   │       ├── "**is** **not** **reading**" / "**has** **not** **arrived**"
│   │       │   │       ├── "**cannot** **read**" / "**will** **not** **come**"
│   │       │   │       └── Negation typically follows auxiliary
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(7) Non-finite VPs**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Infinitival VP:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**to** **read** **books** **carefully**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**to** **have** **been** **reading**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**to** **be** **read**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── Function: Complements, purposes, intentions
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Gerundial VP:**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**reading** **books** **carefully**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**having** **read** **the** **article**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**being** **seen**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── Function: Subjects, objects, complements
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Participial VP:**
│   │       │   │       ├── **Present participle:** "**reading** **books** **every** **day**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Past participle:** "**written** **by** **him**" / "**confused** **and** **lost**"
│   │       │   │       ├── "**having** **completed** **the** **task**"
│   │       │   │       └── Function: Modifiers, reduced clauses
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   └── **(8) Special VP Patterns**
│   │       │       ├── **Phrasal verbs:**
│   │       │       │   ├── "**look** **up**" / "**put** **off**" / "**run** **into**"
│   │       │       │   ├── "**turn** **down** **the** **offer**"
│   │       │       │   └── Verb + particle(s) = single semantic unit
│   │       │       │
│   │       │       ├── **Causative constructions:**
│   │       │       │   ├── "**make** **him** **go**" / "**let** **her** **speak**"
│   │       │       │   ├── "**have** **them** **leave**" / "**get** **it** **done**"
│   │       │       │   └── Verb + object + infinitive
│   │       │       │
│   │       │       ├── **Perception verbs:**
│   │       │       │   ├── "**see** **her** **leave**" / "**hear** **them** **singing**"
│   │       │       │   ├── "**watch** **the** **accident** **happen**"
│   │       │       │   └── Verb + object + bare infinitive/participle
│   │       │       │
│   │       │       └── **Complex predicates:**
│   │       │           ├── "**keep** **reading**" / "**start** **talking**"
│   │       │           ├── "**continue** **studying**" / "**stop** **complaining**"
│   │       │           └── Verb + gerund/infinitive
│   │       │
│   │       ├── **C. c. Adjective Phrase (AP)**
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(1) Basic Structure**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Minimum AP:** Adjective only
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**beautiful**" / "**tall**" / "**happy**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "She is **beautiful**."
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **AP with modifiers:** Intensifier + Adjective
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**very** **beautiful**" / "**quite** **tall**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── "**extremely** **happy**" / "**rather** **sad**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── "**absolutely** **stunning**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Extended AP:** Intensifier + Adjective + Complement
│   │       │   │       ├── "**very** **proud** **of** **him**"
│   │       │   │       ├── "**quite** **aware** **that** **he's** **coming**"
│   │       │   │       └── "**extremely** **difficult** **to** **understand**"
│   │       │   │
│   │       │   ├── **(2) Constituent Elements**
│   │       │   │   ├── **Degree modifier (optional)**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Intensifiers:** "**very**", "**extremely**", "**incredibly**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Downtoners:** "**quite**", "**rather**", "**somewhat**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Approximators:** "**almost**", "**practically**", "**nearly**"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Emphasizers:** "**absolutely**", "**completely**", "**totally**"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Comparatives:** "**much** **more**, **far** **less**"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   ├── **Head Adjective (obligatory)**
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Descriptive adjectives:** "beautiful", "cold", "happy"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Color adjectives:** "red", "blue", "green"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Quality adjectives:** "good", "bad", "interesting"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Size adjectives:** "big", "small", "large"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Age adjectives:** "old", "young", "new"
│   │       │   │   │   ├── **Evaluative adjectives:** "excellent", "awful", "wonderful"
│   │       │   │   │   └── **Comparative/superlative forms:** "more beautiful", "most beautiful"
│   │       │   │   │
│   │       │   │   └── **Complements (depend on adjective)**
│   │       │   │       ├── **Prepositional phrase:** "**proud** **of** **her**" / "**aware** **of** **the** **problem**"
│   │       │   │       ├── **Infinitive clause:** "**easy** **to** **understand**" / "**willing** **to** **help**"
