        │       │   │   │   └── "**If** I had money, I **would buy** a car."
        │       │   │   └── **Type 3 (Unreal Past/Counterfactual):**
        │       │   │       ├── If + past perfect, would have + past participle
        │       │   │       └── "**If** I had known, I **would have helped**."
        │       │   ├── **Unless = If...not:**
        │       │   │   ├── "I won't go **unless you come**." (= if you don't come)
        │       │   │   └── ⚠ NOT used with negatives: ✘ "unless you don't come"
        │       │   ├── **Inversion (Formal - Omitting "if"):**
        │       │   │   ├── "**Had** I known, I would have helped." (= If I had known)
        │       │   │   ├── "**Were** he here, he would agree." (= If he were here)
        │       │   │   └── "**Should** you need help, call me." (= If you should need)
        │       │   └── **Mixed Conditionals:**
        │       │       └── "If I **had studied** (past), I **would have** a job now."
        │       │
        │       ├── **(vi) Concession Clauses**
        │       │   ├── **Subordinators:** although, though, even though, even if, while, whereas, much as, however + adj/adv, no matter + wh-word
        │       │   ├── **Meaning:** Contrast between expectation and reality (X, but still Y)
        │       │   ├── **Examples:**
        │       │   │   ├── "**Although** he tried hard, he failed."
        │       │   │   ├── "**Even though** it was raining, we went out."
        │       │   │   ├── "**While** I understand your point, I disagree."
        │       │   │   ├── "**However hard** she tried, she couldn't succeed."
        │       │   │   ├── "**No matter what** you say, I won't agree."
        │       │   │   └── "**Much as** I like him, I can't trust him."
        │       │   ├── **Differences:**
        │       │   │   ├── **Although/Though:** Standard concession
        │       │   │   ├── **Even though:** Stronger, more emphatic
        │       │   │   ├── **Even if:** Hypothetical concession
        │       │   │   │   └── "**Even if** he apologizes, I won't forgive him." (may not apologize)
        │       │   │   ├── **While/Whereas:** Contrast (often between two facts)
        │       │   │   └── **Though (final position):** "It's expensive, **though**." (informal)
        │       │   └── **Inversion (Formal):**
        │       │       ├── "**Try as he might**, he failed." (= Although he tried)
        │       │       └── "**Much as I admire** her, I disagree."
        │       │
        │       ├── **(vii) Place Clauses**
        │       │   ├── **Subordinators:** where, wherever, everywhere, anywhere
        │       │   ├── **Examples:**
        │       │   │   ├── "Stay **where you are**."
        │       │   │   ├── "Go **wherever you want**."
        │       │   │   ├── "I'll find you **wherever you hide**."
        │       │   │   └── "**Everywhere she went**, people recognized her."
        │       │   └── **Note:** Often overlap with relative clauses
        │       │
        │       ├── **(viii) Manner Clauses**
        │       │   ├── **Subordinators:** as, as if, as though, like (informal), the way (informal)
        │       │   ├── **Examples:**
        │       │   │   ├── "Do it **as I showed you**." (= in the way that)
        │       │   │   ├── "He acts **as if he were king**." (unreal - subjunctive)
        │       │   │   ├── "She looks **as though she hasn't slept**."
        │       │   │   ├── "He talks **like he knows everything**." (informal)
        │       │   │   └── "Do it **the way I taught you**."
        │       │   └── **Subjunctive with "as if/as though" (Unreal):**
        │       │       ├── "He acts as if he **were** (NOT was) the boss."
        │       │       └── "She treats me as though I **didn't** exist."
        │       │
        │       ├── **(ix) Comparison Clauses**
        │       │   ├── **Subordinators:** than, as...as, not so/as...as
        │       │   ├── **Examples:**
        │       │   │   ├── "She is taller **than I am**." (or informal: than me)
        │       │   │   ├── "He works **as hard as she does**."
        │       │   │   ├── "It's not **as easy as it looks**."
        │       │   │   ├── "The more you practice, **the better you get**."
        │       │   │   └── "He is **more intelligent than (he is) brave**."
        │       │   └── **Ellipsis in Comparisons:**
        │       │       ├── "She is smarter than I [am smart]." → "She is smarter than I."
        │       │       └── Often reduced to pronoun only
        │       │
        │       └── **(x) Proportion Clauses**
        │           ├── **Structure:** the + comparative...the + comparative
        │           ├── **Examples:**
        │           │   ├── "**The more** you study, **the more** you learn."
        │           │   ├── "**The harder** he works, **the less** he earns."
        │           │   ├── "**The sooner**, **the better**."
        │           │   └── "**The older** I get, **the wiser** I become."
        │           └── **Note:** Both parts are subordinate to each other (correlative)
        │
        ├── **3. Subordinating Conjunctions (Complete List)**
        │   │
        │   ├── **(a) Simple Subordinators (Single Words)**
        │   │   ├── **Time:** after, before, when, while, since, until, till, once, as
        │   │   ├── **Cause:** because, since, as
        │   │   ├── **Condition:** if, unless
        │   │   ├── **Concession:** although, though, while
        │   │   ├── **Purpose:** lest (formal)
        │   │   ├── **Comparison:** than, as
        │   │   ├── **Manner:** as
        │   │   └── **Place:** where
        │   │
        │   ├── **(b) Complex Subordinators (Multi-word)**
        │   │   ├── **Time:** as soon as, as long as, now that, by the time, every time
        │   │   ├── **Cause:** now that, seeing that, given that, inasmuch as
        │   │   ├── **Condition:** provided (that), providing (that), on condition that, as long as, supposing (that), in case
        │   │   ├── **Concession:** even though, even if, much as, no matter (wh-), however + adj/adv
        │   │   ├── **Purpose:** so that, in order that, so as to, for fear (that)
        │   │   ├── **Result:** so...that, such...that
        │   │   └── **Manner:** as if, as though
        │   │
        │   ├── **(c) Complementizers (Introduce Noun Clauses)**
        │   │   ├── **That:** "I know **that** he left." (often omittable)
        │   │   ├── **If/Whether:** "I wonder **if/whether** he'll come."
        │   │   ├── **Wh-words:** what, who, whom, whose, which, where, when, why, how
        │   │   └── **For (infinitive subject):** "**For** him to leave would be wrong."
        │   │
        │   └── **(d) Relative Words (Introduce Relative Clauses)**
        │       ├── **Pronouns:** who, whom, whose, which, that
        │       ├── **Adverbs:** where, when, why
        │       └── **Determiners:** whose, which (in formal relative clauses)
        │
        ├── **4. Semantic Functions (Meaning Relationships)**
        │   │
        │   ├── **(a) Content/Propositional (What is said/thought/believed)**
        │   │   ├── That-clauses: "I believe **that he is honest**."
        │   │   ├── Wh-clauses: "I wonder **what he wants**."
        │   │   └── Functions as argument of verb (subject, object, complement)
        │   │
        │   ├── **(b) Modification (Describing/Limiting)**
        │   │   ├── **Adjectival:** Describes noun: "The book **that I read**..."
        │   │   └── **Adverbial:** Describes verb/clause: "He left **because he was tired**."
        │   │
        │   ├── **(c) Circumstance (Setting context for main clause)**
        │   │   ├── Time: "**When I arrived**, he left."
        │   │   ├── Place: "**Where there's smoke**, there's fire."
        │   │   ├── Manner: "Do it **as I showed you**."
        │   │   └── Circumstantial clauses often initial
        │   │
        │   ├── **(d) Contingency (Conditions for main clause)**
        │   │   ├── Condition: "**If it rains**, stay home."
        │   │   ├── Concession: "**Although tired**, he continued."
        │   │   ├── Purpose: "Study **so that you pass**."
        │   │   └── Result: "He was **so tired that** he slept."
        │   │
        │   └── **(e) Elaboration (Additional/Explanatory Information)**
        │       ├── Non-restrictive relatives: "John, **who is tall**, plays basketball."
        │       ├── Apposition: "The fact **that he lied**..."
        │       └── Adds information without essential identification
        │
        ├── **5. Structural Forms of Subordinate Clauses**
        │   │
        │   ├── **(a) Finite Clauses (With tensed verb)**
        │   │   ├── **Definition:** Contains a verb marked for tense (past/present)
        │   │   ├── **Structure:** Subordinator + Subject + Finite Verb + (Complements)
        │   │   ├── **Examples:**
        │   │   │   ├── "I know that he **is** coming." (present)
        │   │   │   ├── "She left because she **was** tired." (past)
        │   │   │   ├── "If he **comes**, tell him." (present for future)
        │   │   │   └── "The book that I **read** was good." (past)
        │   │   └── **Tense in Subordinate Clauses:**
        │   │       ├── May differ from main clause: "I know he **left**."
        │   │       ├── Backshifting in reported speech: "He said he **was** tired."
        │   │       └── Present for future in time/condition clauses
        │   │
        │   ├── **(b) Non-finite Clauses (Without tense marking)**
        │   │   │
        │   │   ├── **(i) Infinitive Clauses (to + V)**
        │   │   │   ├── **Subject:** "**To err** is human."
        │   │   │   ├── **Object:** "I want **to leave**."
        │   │   │   ├── **Complement:** "Her goal is **to win**."
        │   │   │   ├── **Purpose:** "I came **to help**."
        │   │   │   ├── **Result:** "He was too tired **to continue**."
        │   │   │   ├── **With subject (for + NP + to):** "I want **for him to leave**."
        │   │   │   └── **After adjectives:** "I'm happy **to help**."
        │   │   │
        │   │   ├── **(ii) Gerund-Participle Clauses (-ing)**
        │   │   │   ├── **Subject:** "**Running daily** keeps you fit."
        │   │   │   ├── **Object:** "I enjoy **reading books**."
        │   │   │   ├── **Adverbial (participle):** "**Walking home**, I saw him."
        │   │   │   ├── **Reduced relative:** "The man **standing there**..."
        │   │   │   ├── **After preposition:** "He left without **saying goodbye**."
        │   │   │   └── **Supplementive:** "**Being tired**, he slept early."
        │   │   │
        │   │   └── **(iii) Past Participle Clauses (-ed/-en)**
        │   │       ├── **Reduced relative (passive):** "The book **written by her**..."
        │   │       ├── **Adverbial:** "**Tired from work**, he slept early."
        │   │       ├── **After conjunction:** "**When asked**, he confessed."
        │   │       └── **Supplementive:** "**Exhausted**, she collapsed."
        │   │
        │   ├── **(c) Verbless Clauses (No verb at all)**
        │   │   ├── **Definition:** Reduced clause with verb (usually "be") deleted
        │   │   ├── **Examples:**
        │   │   │   ├── "**Although tired**, he continued." (= Although he was tired)
        │   │   │   ├── "**When in Rome**, do as Romans do." (= When you are in Rome)
        │   │   │   ├── "**If possible**, send it today." (= If it is possible)
        │   │   │   ├── "**Once finished**, submit the report." (= Once it is finished)
        │   │   │   └── "He stood there, **speechless**." (= being speechless)
        │   │   └── **Common patterns:**
        │   │       ├── Subordinator + Adjective: "although tired, if necessary"
        │   │       ├── Subordinator + PP: "when in doubt, while at home"
        │   │       └── Subordinator + past participle: "once finished, when asked"
        │   │
        │   └── **(d) Position of Subordinate Clauses**
        │       │
        │       ├── **(i) Initial (Before Main Clause)**
        │       │   ├── **Common for:** Adverbial clauses (time, condition, concession)
        │       │   ├── **Examples:**
        │       │   │   ├── "**Although it rained**, we went out."
        │       │   │   ├── "**If you see him**, tell him."
        │       │   │   ├── "**When I arrived**, he left."
        │       │   │   └── "**Because she was ill**, she stayed home."
        │       │   ├── **Punctuation:** COMMA after initial subordinate clause
        │       │   └── **Effect:** Sets scene, provides context, emphasizes condition
        │       │
        │       ├── **(ii) Medial (Inserted within Main Clause)**
        │       │   ├── **Common for:** Non-restrictive relative clauses
        │       │   ├── **Examples:**
        │       │   │   ├── "My brother**, who lives abroad,** called yesterday."
        │       │   │   ├── "The report**, which was due today,** is incomplete."
        │       │   │   └── "Paris**, where I studied,** is beautiful."
        │       │   ├── **Punctuation:** COMMAS on both sides (parenthetical)
        │       │   └── **Effect:** Adds supplementary information
        │       │
        │       └── **(iii) Final (After Main Clause)**
        │           ├── **Common for:** All types (default position for many)
        │           ├── **Examples:**
        │           │   ├── "He stayed home **because he was ill**."
        │           │   ├── "I know **that she left**."
        │           │   ├── "This is the book **that I read**."
        │           │   └── "I'll call you **when I arrive**."
        │           ├── **Punctuation:**
        │           │   ├── NO comma for restrictive clauses
        │           │   ├── COMMA for non-restrictive (if final, rare)
        │           │   └── NO comma for essential adverbials ("because" clauses)
        │           └── **Effect:** Provides explanation, elaboration, identification
        │
        ├── **6. Grammatical Rules & Constraints**
        │   │
        │   ├── **(a) Tense Rules in Subordinate Clauses**
        │   │   ├── **Future Time in Time/Condition Clauses:**
        │   │   │   ├── Use PRESENT (not will) for future meaning
        │   │   │   ├── ✔ "When he **arrives**, I'll leave."
        │   │   │   ├── ✘ "When he **will arrive**, I'll leave."
        │   │   │   ├── ✔ "If it **rains**, we'll stay home."
        │   │   │   └── ✘ "If it **will rain**, we'll stay home."
        │   │   ├── **Backshifting (Reported Speech):**
        │   │   │   ├── Move tense one step back in reported clauses
        │   │   │   ├── "He said, 'I **am** tired.'" → "He said he **was** tired."
        │   │   │   ├── "She said, 'I **have** finished.'" → "She said she **had** finished."
        │   │   │   └── Exceptions: Universal truths, immediately relevant
        │   │   └── **Sequence of Tenses:**
        │   │       ├── Past main verb often requires past subordinate
        │   │       ├── "I knew that he **was** (NOT is) tired."
        │   │       └── Exception: Still-true statements may keep present
        │   │
        │   ├── **(b) Mood Rules (Subjunctive)**
        │   │   ├── **Mandative Subjunctive (after verbs of demand/recommendation):**
        │   │   │   ├── Use base form (no -s, no past)
        │   │   │   ├── ✔ "I demand that he **be** present."
        │   │   │   ├── ✔ "She insisted that he **leave**." (NOT leaves)
        │   │   │   └── Verbs: demand, insist, suggest, recommend, require, request
        │   │   ├── **Formulaic Subjunctive (Fixed expressions):**
        │   │   │   ├── "**Be** that as it may..."
        │   │   │   ├── "**Come** what may..."
        │   │   │   ├── "Long **live** the king!"
        │   │   │   └── "If need **be**..."
        │   │   └── **Hypothetical Subjunctive (Unreal conditions):**
        │   │       ├── "If I **were** (NOT was) rich..." (formal)
        │   │       ├── "He acts as if he **were** the boss."
        │   │       └── "I wish I **were** there."
        │   │
        │   ├── **(c) Word Order in Embedded Questions**
        │   │   ├── **Rule:** Use STATEMENT word order (S + V), NOT question inversion
        │   │   ├── **Correct:**
        │   │   │   ├── ✔ "I wonder what **he wants**."
        │   │   │   ├── ✔ "Tell me where **she lives**."
        │   │   │   ├── ✔ "I don't know why **he left**."
        │   │   │   └── ✔ "Ask him if **he can come**."
        │   │   └── **Incorrect:**
        │   │       ├── ✘ "I wonder what **does he want**."
        │   │       ├── ✘ "Tell me where **does she live**."
        │   │       └── ✘ "Ask him **can he** come."
        │   │
        │   ├── **(d) Punctuation Rules**
        │   │   ├── **Initial Adverbial Clause:** Comma required
        │   │   │   └── "**Although tired,** he continued."
        │   │   ├── **Final Adverbial Clause:** Usually no comma
        │   │   │   └── "He continued **although he was tired**."
        │   │   ├── **Restrictive Relative Clause:** NO commas
        │   │   │   └── "The book **that I read** was good."
        │   │   ├── **Non-Restrictive Relative Clause:** COMMAS required
        │   │   │   └── "Paris**, which I love,** is beautiful."
        │   │   └── **Noun Clauses:** Usually no comma
        │   │       └── "I know **that he left**."
        │   │
        │   └── **(e) Reduction Rules (Shortening Clauses)**
        │       ├── **Relative Clause Reduction:**
        │       │   ├── Delete who/which/that + be → keep participle
        │       │   ├── "The man **who is standing** → **standing**..."
        │       │   └── "The book **that was written** → **written**..."
        │       ├── **Adverbial Clause Reduction:**
        │       │   ├── Delete subject + be (if same as main subject)
        │       │   ├── "**While he was walking**, he saw..." → "**While walking**, he saw..."
        │       │   └── "**Although she was tired**, she continued." → "**Although tired**, she continued."
        │       └── **Condition for Reduction:**
        │           ├── Same subject in both clauses, OR
        │           └── Impersonal subject (it is...)
        │
        ├── **7. Common Exam Traps & Errors**
        │   │
        │   ├── **(a) Inverted Word Order in Embedded Questions**
        │   │   ├── ✘ "I wonder what **does she** want." → ✔ "...what **she wants**."
        │   │   ├── ✘ "Tell me where **is he** going." → ✔ "...where **he is** going."
        │   │   └── ✘ "Ask him **can he** come." → ✔ "...if **he can** come."
        │   │
        │   ├── **(b) Will in Time/Condition Clauses**
        │   │   ├── ✘ "When he **will arrive**, call me." → ✔ "When he **arrives**, call me."
        │   │   ├── ✘ "If it **will rain**, stay home." → ✔ "If it **rains**, stay home."
        │   │   └── ✘ "Before she **will leave**, say goodbye." → ✔ "Before she **leaves**, say goodbye."
        │   │
        │   ├── **(c) "That" in Non-Restrictive Clauses**
        │   │   ├── ✘ "Paris, **that** I love, is beautiful." → ✔ "Paris, **which** I love, is beautiful."
        │   │   ├── ✘ "My brother, **that** lives abroad, called." → ✔ "My brother, **who** lives abroad, called."
        │   │   └── **Rule:** "That" ONLY for restrictive clauses
        │   │
        │   ├── **(d) Omitting Relative Pronoun (When Not Allowed)**
        │   │   ├── ✘ "The man **Ø** called left." (subject - CANNOT omit)
        │   │   │   └── ✔ "The man **who/that** called left."
        │   │   ├── ✘ "Paris, **Ø** I love, is beautiful." (non-restrictive - CANNOT omit)
        │   │   │   └── ✔ "Paris, **which** I love, is beautiful."
        │   │   └── ✔ "The book **Ø** I read was good." (object in restrictive - CAN omit)
        │   │
        │   ├── **(e) If vs. Whether**
        │   │   ├── ✘ "I'm uncertain about **if** to go." → ✔ "...about **whether** to go."
        │   │   ├── ✘ "**If or not** he comes..." → ✔ "**Whether or not** he comes..."
        │   │   └── **Rule:** Use "whether" after prepositions and with "or not" directly following
        │   │
        │   ├── **(f) Subjunctive Errors**
        │   │   ├── ✘ "I insist that he **goes**." → ✔ "I insist that he **go**."
        │   │   ├── ✘ "She suggested that he **leaves**." → ✔ "...that he **leave**."
        │   │   └── ✘ "If I **was** rich..." (formal) → ✔ "If I **were** rich..."
        │   │
        │   ├── **(g) Comma Errors with Relative Clauses**
        │   │   ├── ✘ "The book, that I read, was good." (commas with restrictive)
        │   │   │   └── ✔ "The book that I read was good."
        │   │   ├── ✘ "My brother who lives abroad called." (no commas with non-restrictive)
        │   │   │   └── ✔ "My brother, who lives abroad, called."
        │   │   └── **Meaning change:**
        │   │       ├── "My brother**s** who live abroad called." (restrictive - some brothers)
        │   │       └── "My brother, who lives abroad, called." (non-restrictive - one brother)
        │   │
        │   └── **(h) Fragment Errors (Subordinate Clause Alone)**
        │       ├── ✘ "**Because he was tired.**" (fragment - incomplete)
        │       │   └── ✔ "He left **because he was tired**."
        │       ├── ✘ "**Although she tried hard.**" (fragment)
        │       │   └── ✔ "**Although she tried hard**, she failed."
        │       └── **Rule:** Subordinate clause CANNOT stand alone as a sentence
        │
        └── **8. Competitive Exam Summary**
            │
            ├── **Key Concepts:**
            │   ├── **Subordination = Unequal elements** (main + dependent)
            │   ├── **3 Types of Subordinate Clauses:**
            │   │   ├── **Nominal:** Subject, Object, Complement
            │   │   ├── **Adjectival (Relative):** Modify nouns
            │   │   └── **Adverbial:** Time, Reason, Condition, etc.
            │   └── **Subordinators:** Conjunctions, Complementizers, Relative words
            │
            ├── **Essential Rules:**
            │   ├── **(1) No "will" in time/condition clauses:** "When he arrives" (NOT will arrive)
            │   ├── **(2) Statement order in embedded questions:** "I wonder what he wants"
            │   ├── **(3) "That" only for restrictive:** Paris, which (NOT that) I love
            │   ├── **(4) Comma for non-restrictive:** "John, who is tall, plays basketball"
            │   ├── **(5) No comma for restrictive:** "The man that called left"
            │   └── **(6) Subjunctive after demand/insist/suggest:** "I insist that he go"
            │
            ├── **Relative Pronoun Quick Guide:**
            │   ├── **Who:** Subject (people)
            │   ├── **Whom:** Object (people, formal)
            │   ├── **Which:** Things (non-restrictive only for things)
            │   ├── **That:** Restrictive only (people/things)
            │   ├── **Whose:** Possessive (people/things)
            │   └── **Ø (Zero):** Object only, restrictive only
            │
            ├── **Subordinator Categories:**
            │   ├── **Time:** when, before, after, until, while, since, as soon as
            │   ├── **Reason:** because, since, as, now that
            │   ├── **Condition:** if, unless, provided that, as long as
            │   ├── **Concession:** although, though, even though, even if
            │   ├── **Purpose:** so that, in order that, to
            │   ├── **Result:** so...that, such...that
            │   └── **Comparison:** than, as...as
            │
            └── **Quick Tests:**
                ├── **Restrictive vs. Non-restrictive:** Does removing the clause change WHICH noun is meant?
                ├── **Finite vs. Non-finite:** Is there a tensed verb (was/is)?
                ├── **Omit relative pronoun?:** Object + Restrictive = Yes; Subject/Non-restrictive = No
                └── **Will allowed?:** Not in time/condition clauses for future meaning

---

## 📋 QUICK FIXES FOR COMMON MISTAKES

### **TOP 10 SENTENCE STRUCTURE ERRORS:**

| **Error Type** | **❌ Wrong** | **✅ Correct** | **Explanation** |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Word order in questions** | I wonder where is she. | I wonder where she is. | Indirect questions = statement word order |
| **"That" in non-restrictive** | My brother, that lives here | My brother, who lives here | Use who/which for non-restrictive only |
| **Missing commas** | My brother who lives in Paris is here | My brother, who lives in Paris, is here | Non-restrictive = needs commas |
| **Extra commas** | The book, that I read, was good | The book that I read was good | Restrictive = no commas |
| **Will in time clause** | When he will arrive... | When he arrives... | Simple present for future time clauses |
| **Wrong subjunctive** | I demand that she is here | I demand that she be here | Subjunctive after demand/insist/suggest |
| **Comma splice** | She sang, he danced. | She sang, and he danced. | Need coordinator between independent clauses |
| **Run-on sentence** | She sang he danced. | She sang, and he danced. | Independent clauses need connector |
| **Dangling modifier** | Walking to school, the rain started. | While I was walking to school, the rain started. | Modifier subject must match sentence subject |
| **Unclear antecedent** | John told Mark that he was lazy. | John told Mark that Mark was lazy. | Pronoun reference must be crystal clear |

### **KEY DISTINCTION: RESTRICTIVE vs. NON-RESTRICTIVE CLAUSES**

**Restrictive (Defining):**
- Essential information
- Identifies WHICH noun
- ❌ No commas
- Can delete "that" if object
- "The book **that** I bought is excellent." (specific book)

**Non-Restrictive (Non-defining):**
- Extra information
- Noun already identified
- ✅ **Must have commas**
- Cannot delete relative pronoun
- "My book, **which** I bought yesterday, is excellent." (I have one book)

---

## 🎯 EXAM-FOCUSED CHECKLIST

Before submitting written work, verify:

- [ ] All independent clauses properly connected (comma + coordinator OR semicolon)
- [ ] Noun clauses have correct word order (statement order, not question inversion)
- [ ] "That" is only used in restrictive clauses
- [ ] Non-restrictive clauses have commas AND use who/whom/which/where/when
- [ ] Subjunctive is used after demand/insist/recommend/suggest
- [ ] Time/condition clauses use simple present for future meaning
- [ ] Relative pronouns match antecedent (who=people, which=things)
- [ ] Infinitive and gerund complements match verb type
- [ ] Parallelism in compound structures
- [ ] No dangling or misplaced modifiers
- [ ] Pronouns have clear antecedents

---

## 📚 STUDY TIPS

1. **Practice identifying clauses first** - Mark every finite verb = you found potential clauses
2. **Ask "Can it stand alone?"** - Independent clause = yes; Dependent = no
3. **Check for commas near relative pronouns** - This usually tells you restrictive vs. non-restrictive
4. **Substitute pronouns to test** - "The students who study hard" = "They study hard" ✓
5. **Create flashcards** - Make cards for problematic subordinators and their rules
6. **Do sentence combining** - Join simple sentences using different clause types
7. **Study authentic examples** - Read well-written articles and mark the clause structures
